HD Danske Bank Swings To 4Q Net Loss On Goodwill Writedown
BY By Anna Molin
WC 409 words
PD 3 February 2015
ET 02:39
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright 2015, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

Denmark's biggest lender Danske Bank A/S (DANSKE.KO) Tuesday hiked its dividend for the full year and said its strong capital position would allow it to launch a share buy-back program in 2015, despite swinging to a fourth quarter net loss following a hefty goodwill writedown.

TD 

The Copenhagen-based bank said it swung to a net loss of 6.29 billion Danish kroner ($956.7 million) in the three months to Dec. 31, compared to a net profit of 1.92 billion kronor in the year-earlier period. Analysts had expected a net loss of 6 billion kroner, according to estimates from financial information provider SIX.

Quarterly net interest income increased to 5.88 billion kroner from 5.68 billion kroner a year ago while quarterly loan losses rose to 853 million kroner from 845 million kroner in the same period a year earlier.

Danske in December said it would book a goodwill writedown of 9 billion kronor for 2014 as pressure on earnings from low interest rates undermined the value of some of its assets. The impairments are based on long-term assessments and relate to activities in Finland, Northern Ireland and Estonia.

Denmark's largest bank has been cutting costs, shedding staff and shut down unprofitable retail banking operations in Ireland to cover losses suffered following the 2008 financial crisis.

The bank said it expects a net profit above 14 billion kronor and expenses below 22 billion kronor in 2015.

The board proposed a dividend of 5.5 per share or 43% of net profit before goodwill writedowns, a big jump compared to its year-earlier dividend of 2 kroner per share or 28% of net profit. It also said the bank would launch a 5 billion kronor share buy-back program in 2015.

The common equity Tier 1 ratio -- a measure of financial strength -- stood at 15.1% at the end of the year, up from 14.7% a year ago.

"We will continue to review our business and take new initiatives to ensure a return on shareholders' equity of above 12.5% in 2018 at the latest," the bank's Chief Executive Thomas Borgen and Chairman Ole Andersen said in a joint statement.

-Write to Anna Molin at anna.molin@wsj.com; Twitter: @AnnaWSJ

(END) Dow Jones Newswires

February 03, 2015 02:39 ET (07:39 GMT)

HD Danske Bank's FY net profit in Lithuania falls to EUR 9.4 mln
WC 327 words
PD 3 February 2015
ET 05:00
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Baltic News Service

LP 

(expands)

VILNIUS, Feb 03, BNS - The Lithuanian branch of Danske Bank, the second-biggest financial group in Northern Europe by assets, on Tuesday posted a net profit of 9.385 million euros for the full year 2014, down from 27.144 million euros in 2013.

TD 

The decline in net profit was due to a significant decrease in reversals of provisions for loans and off-balance sheet items, to 643,200 euros in 2014, from 18.257 million euros in 2013, the branch said in its 2014 performance report.

"Last year was a very important year not only for the country's banking sector, but also to the state as a whole. Businesses very actively prepared themselves for the changeover to the European single currency," the branch's CEO, Gintautas Galvanauskas, said in a press release.

"The fact that Lithuania became the 19th member of the eurozone is likely to encourage even greater interest from foreign investors in our market," he said.

Danske Bank's Lithuanian branch this year plans to increase its focus on services to business clients and to pay special attention to private banking clients and customers with a high need for complex banking services, the CEO said.

The branch's assets increased by 259.061 million euros, or 25.5 percent, over the year to reach 1.765 billion euros in late December. The net loan portfolio, which makes up more than half of the assets, totaled 917.511 million euros at the end of December, down by 1.2 percent from a year ago.

The deposit portfolio soared by 30.4 percent last year compared with 2013 to 1.155 billion euros.

In Lithuania, Danske Bank also has a leasing subsidiary, Danske Lizingas, as well as asset management operations (Danske Capital) and financial market operations (Danske Markets Lithuania).

Vilnius newsroom, verslas@bns.lt, +370 5 205 8520

HD Estonian unit of Danske Bank sees profit shrink 52 pct to EUR 22.7 mln in 2014
WC 313 words
PD 3 February 2015
ET 05:32
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Baltic News Service

LP 

TALLINN, Feb 03, BNS Danske Bank made a net profit of 22.7 million euros in Estonia last year compared to the year-earlier 47.3 million euros.

"Danske Bank continued to increase its business volumes in both the corporate banking and personal banking segments while maintaining high customer satisfaction and acceptable profitability in spite of a challenging environment in 2014," CEO of the Danske operation in Estonia Aivar Rehe said.

TD 

The Estonian bank's return on allocated capital was 29.8 percent compared to 61.1 percent in 2013. The decline was mostly due to lower income of 55.8 million euros (a year earlier 72.5 million euros) resulting from decreases in net trading income and net interest income. Trading income was affected by the bank's decision to lower its risk profile, which resulted in lower activity, while net interest income was affected by a change in the group's internal funds transfer pricing, Rehe said.

The bank's profit before loan impairment charges dropped to 21.3 million euros from 44 million euos in 2013.

Operating income, at 55.8 million euros, was 16.7 million euros smaller than the year before. Operating expenses at the same time increased by 6 million euros to 34.5 million euros.

The bank earned 29 million euros of interest income compared to 33.7 million euros a year earlier. Net fee income declined to 18.1 million euros from 19 million euros in 2013.

The loan portfolio stood at 1.25 billion euros at the end of 2014 compared to 1.14 billion euros at the end of 2013.

The bank had 101,500 customers at the end of the reporting period.

Tallinn newsroom, +372 610 8821, majandus@bns.ee

Baltic News Service

HD Danske Bank CEO sees negative rates for a year
WC 137 words
PD 3 February 2015
ET 04:47
SN Reuters News
SC LBA
LA English
CY Copyright 2015 Thomson Reuters. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

COPENHAGEN, Feb 3 (Reuters) - Danske Bank's Chief Executive Thomas Borgen said on Tuesday he expected negative interest rates set by the Danish central bank to last for a year and the bank would not charge retail customers to deposit their cash.

"We do not expect negative interest rates will continue for a long time. As far as it is ever possible, we must protect our customers. We do not want them to have a negative rate on their wage account," Borgen said via a live interpreter, adding he expected negative rates to last for a year.

TD 

"If the situation continues for years, we would need to reassess," he told a news conference. (Reporting by Sabina Zawadzki, editing by Terje Solsvik)

HD Latvian branch of Danske Bank posts EUR 1.2 mln loss for 2014
WC 529 words
PD 3 February 2015
ET 05:50
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Baltic News Service

LP 

RIGA, Feb 03, BNS - The Latvian branch of Danske Bank closed last year with a loss of 1.202 million euros as opposed to a profit in 2013, BNS was told at the bank.

The total income of the Latvian branch of Danske Bank in 2014 was 8.8 million euros, up 19 percent from 2013, and the profit before loan impairment charges was 3.7 million euros, which was a double increase from the year before.

TD 

The banks representatives said that, in line with the conservative risk policy of the Danske Bank group, provisions in the amount of 7.9 million euros were created at the beginning last year which was consistent with the effects of the worst geopolitical scenario on the economy but the provisions were gradually reduced with amortization of the mortgage loan portfolio. Regardless of the comparatively large provisions, the bank managed to cut its loss substantially in 2014, they said.

The net interest income of the Latvian branch of Danske Bank last year grew 28 percent, and net fee income rose 2.4 times year-on-year. "Other income shrank 26 percent and, as this income is mostly related to sale of the banks properties, we expect its further reduction in the coming quarters, the banks representatives said.

The banks expenses dropped 8 percent in 2014.

Deposits held by the Latvian branch of Danske Bank increased 51 percent, reaching 331.1 million euros at the end of 2014, and the loan portfolio grew 17 percent to 356.9 million euros.

The amount of loans issued to business customers rose 43 percent last year to 225.6 million euros. New business customer loans issued in 2014 totalled 102.3 million euros.

The Latvian branch of Danske Bank is now working on development of leasing services to be offered to business customers in future.

"Danske Banks goal in the Baltic states is to become the bank offering the best service to business customers. To this end, around 15 million euros will be invested in development of business customers service in the next two years," the banks representatives said, adding that part of the money will be used to develop a joint IT platform for Danske Bank in the three Baltic states that will be largely integrated in the systems of the Danske Bank group.

"I am glad that last year we succeeded in increasing significantly loans to business customers. This year we will continue the efforts to expand services to business customers and will start offering leasing services to business customers in the second half of the year, said Raivis Kakanis, the head of the Latvian branch of Danske Bank.

The Latvian branch of Danske Bank closed 2013 with a profit of 2.94 million euros.

The Latvian branch of Danske Bank became part of the Danish Danske Bank Group in 2007. At the end of September 2014, the Latvian branch of Danske Bank ranked 15th among the banks operating in Latvia in terms of assets.

Riga newsroom, +371 6708 8606, eko_zinas@ bns.lv

HD Danske Bank set to exit personal banking operations in Baltics
WC 358 words
PD 3 February 2015
ET 06:14
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Baltic News Service

LP 

VILNIUS, Feb 03, BNS - Danske Bank, the second-biggest financial group in Northern Europe by assets, has decided to gradually phase out its personal banking operations in the Baltic countries and to focus on business customers from the start of this year.

Danske Bank unveiled a new strategy for its Baltics operations in its 2014 annual report released on Tuesday.

TD 

"Our current personal customer operations in the Baltics do not have sufficient scale to generate an acceptable return, and we do not foresee a turnaround to a sustainable profitability level. We have therefore decided to exit our personal banking operations and are considering various options," the bank said.

"We will honor our obligations to service our current customer base, and the exit could therefore last for several years. The number of branches and the headcount will be reduced. From 1 January 2015, the personal banking activities will be presented as non-core operations," it said.

Gintautas Galvanauskas, CEO of Danske Bank's Lithuanian branch, said in a press release, "We always strive to provide the highest value to our business customers. According to Danske Bank's renewed strategy for the Baltic countries, this year we will put even more our focus on services to businesses and will increase our activity in this segment."

"In 2015, we have an ambitious goal of increasing our business customer portfolio by up to 10 percent," he said.

Danske Bank is planning to invest around 15 million euros in its Baltic units over the next two years. A part of the investment will go toward the development of a common IT platform. The bank expects that its profitability in the region will increase following the shift of focus to business customers.

Danske Bank's Lithuanian branch last year saw its net profit slump down to 9.385 million euros, from 27.144 million euros in 2013. The branch's assets increased by 259.061 million euros, or 25.5 percent, over the year to reach 1.765 billion euros in late December.

Vilnius newsroom, verslas@bns.lt, +370 5 205 8520

HD Danish negative rates could cost Danske Bank up to $137 mln
WC 128 words
PD 3 February 2015
ET 05:45
SN Reuters News
SC LBA
LA English
CY Copyright 2015 Thomson Reuters. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

COPENHAGEN, Feb 3 (Reuters) - The Danish central bank's certificate of deposit rate of -0.5 percent will cost Danske Bank 700 to 900 million Danish crowns ($107 to 137 million) annually, Chief Executive Thomas Borgen told Reuters.

"The rate cut from minus 5 basis point to minus 50 basis point, all things be equal, has a cost of between 700 and 900 million for Danske Bank," Borgen said after the bank issued its full-year results.

TD 

"That's before we initiate mitigating actions and pass some of it through to institutional and business clients," he said.

($1 = 6.5608 Danish crowns) (Reporting by Ole Mikkelsen; editing by Sabina Zawadzki)

HD Danske Bank outlines DKr5bn share buyback
BY Richard Milne, Nordic Correspondent
WC 472 words
PD 3 February 2015
ET 08:29
SN Financial Times (FT.Com)
SC FTCMA
LA English
CY Copyright 2015 The Financial Times Ltd. All rights reserved. Please do not cut and paste FT articles and redistribute by email or post to the web.

LP 

Danske Bank unveiled plans for its first share buyback in more than a decade and a higher than expected dividend after Denmark's biggest lender posted mixed results.

Danske announced on Tuesday it would buy back up to DKr5bn ($764m) of shares this year while paying out DKr5.50 per share in dividends, slightly ahead of analysts' expectations.

TD 

But some analysts were disappointed by slightly lower than expected fourth-quarter results and what they saw as relatively weak forecasts for this year.

Danske has struggled more than the other big Nordic banks to put the global financial crisis behind it as its exposure in its home country and Ireland has weighed it down. Denmark was hit hardest of the four big Nordic countries by the crisis and is still one of the only European countries in which banks have been allowed to fail in recent years.

Denmark's biggest bank changed its chief executive in 2013 and reinstated its dividend last year in an attempt to boost its standing with investors, who have tended to favour the four big Swedish banks - all of which came through the financial crisis in stronger shape.

Net profit in the fourth quarter before goodwill impairment charges fell from DKr3.3bn a year earlier to DKr2.8bn. Including goodwill writedowns of DKr9.1bn due to Danske's business in Finland, Northern Ireland and Estonia - already announced in December - the bank made a net loss of DKr6.3bn in the quarter compared with a profit of DKr3.3bn a year earlier.

For the full year it made a net profit of DKr3.8bn and one of DKr12.9bn excluding the goodwill impairments. Danske said it expected to make a net profit of more than DKr14bn this year, but that is below consensus analyst forecasts of DKr15.4bn.

"2015 guidance [is] disappointing: the new financial targets lack ambition and critically there is no big cost ambition. The dividend is small appeasement," wrote Nick Anderson, analyst at Berenberg, the German investment bank.

Danske also raised its return on equity targets slightly from 9 to 9.5 per cent for this year and from 12 to 12.5 per cent by 2018. It also tweaked its dividend policy from aiming to pay out about 40 per cent of net profits - it paid out 43 per cent of last year's before goodwill - to 40-50 per cent in the future.

But that still lags behind Swedish banks with Nordea, the Nordic region's biggest bank, paying out 70 per cent of its net profits and Swedbank aiming for as much as three-quarters.

Danske's shares slipped 0.8 per cent to DKr170.90 in afternoon trading on Tuesday, having risen more than 38 per cent over the past 12 months.

HD Danske Bank profits plunge on goodwill writedown
WC 306 words
PD 3 February 2015
ET 09:26
SN Agence France Presse
SC AFPR
LA English
CY Copyright Agence France-Presse, 2015 All reproduction and presentation rights reserved.

LP 

Denmark's largest bank, Danske Bank, on Tuesday reported a 46 percent drop in annual profits as it wrote down the value of some operations due to macroeconomic factors.

"The macroeconomic environment did not offer much support as the year saw a continuation of low interest rate levels and slow growth," chief executive Thomas Borgen and chairman Ole Andersen said in a joint statement.

TD 

"Despite this, we managed to increase the topline (gross sales) across our business as a result of a firm focus on delivering value to customers," they added.

Net profit was in line with analysts' expectations, falling 46 percent to 3.58 billion kroner (481 million euros, $545 million) as revenue grew 10 percent to 43.87 billion kroner.

The company in December announced that it would write down the goodwill valuation of its operations in Finland, Northern Ireland and Estonia.

Excluding an estimated 9.1 billion kroner for goodwill impairment blamed on "expected weaker long-term macroeconomic developments", profits rose 82 percent to 12.9 billion kroner.

The goodwill valuation represents the difference between a company's assets and what a potential buyer would be willing to pay for it.

In 2015, the group expects net profit to exceed 14 billion kroner.

Net interest income rose five percent "despite persistently low interest rates", while loan impairment charges fell 32 percent, the bank said.

Danske Bank has been cutting costs since Denmark became the worst-hit Scandinavian country in the 2008 financial crisis, and the group has struggled to keep pace with rival Nordic banking group Nordea.

The Copenhagen-based bank said it had decided to scrap its personal banking operations in the Baltics since the business did not have "sufficient scale to generate an acceptable return".

HD "Danske Bank" posts EUR 1.2 million in net losses in 2014
BY Airisa damsone
WC 456 words
PD 3 February 2015
ET 09:36
SN Latvian News Agency
SC LETA
LA English
CY (c) 2015 LETA .

LP 

RIGA, Feb 3 (LETA) - "Danske Bank" in Latvia posted EUR 1.2 million in net losses last year, whereas in 2013, the bank had earned a profit of EUR 2.94 million.Last year, "Danske Bank" in Latvia doubled profit before provisions for impaired loans, which amounted to EUR 3.7 million, the bank said in a statement to the media. However, pursuant to "Danske Bank" group's conservative risk policy, the bank put aside EUR 7.9 million at the beginning of last year, reflecting the effect that a worst-case geopolitical scenario could have on the economy of Latvia. The bank believes that its operational results were very good last year, as the amount of losses was reduced significantly in 2014 regardless of the comparatively large amount of provisions. The net result, however, was negative.Deposits at the bank increased 51 percent to EUR 33.1 million at the end of 2014.The bank's loan portfolio increased 17 percent to EUR 356.9 million.

TD 

The amount of loans issued to companies grew 43 percent, amounting to EUR 225.6 million at the end of 2014. The bank issued a total of EUR 102.3 million in loans to start-ups last year. "Danske Bank" is resolved to continue expanding its share of the corporate customer segment, offering its clients professional consulting and individual borrowing solutions. In the latter part of the year, the bank will begin to offer leasing services to its corporate clients, said "Danske Bank" head in Latvia, Raivis Kakanis.The bank's total income rose 19 percent to EUR 8.8 million last year. Net interest income increased 28 percent to EUR 5.097 million, whereas net commissions grew 138 percent to EUR 2.079 million. Other incomes decreased 26 percent. The bank continued to pursue diligent cost supervision policy last year, as a result, "Danske Bank" costs in Latvia reduced 8 percent last year.The income to expenditure ratio last year was 58.2 percent, down from 75 percent in 2013."Danske Bank" has one customer service center in Latvia, which employs 94 people."Danske Bank" has set itself an objective of becoming the best bank in the Baltics in terms of corporate customer service. To attain the goal, the bank will invest about EUR 15 million in the development of corporate customer services during the next two years. Part of the investment will go into the development of a pan-Baltic IT platform to provide modern and uniform range of services to the bank's corporate customers in the Baltic countries."Danske Bank" is the Latvian branch of the Denmark-registered "Danske Bank".

HD Danske Bank to downsize personal banking services in Baltics
WC 302 words
PD 3 February 2015
ET 09:46
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Baltic News Service

LP 

(specifies, adds para. 3)

RIGA, Feb 03, BNS - Danish banking group Danske Bank will gradually downsize personal banking services in the Baltic states, including Latvia, and will focus on corporate customers.

TD 

This will be done in line with Danske Bank's new strategy in the Baltic states, the bank said in its annual report published on Tuesday.

"Danske Bank is going to significantly downsize services to personal customers in the Baltic states in the coming years. This is the strategy we have been implementing in Latvia for several years already, Ieva Zaure, the spokeswoman of the Latvian branch of Danske Bank, told BNS, underlining that the bank would continue serving individual customers alongside the services to business customers.

Danske Bank explained t he decision to downsize personal banking operations in the Baltic states with insufficient profit from this particular segment.

Our current personal customer operations in the Baltics do not have sufficient scale to generate an acceptable return, and we do not foresee a turnaround to a sustainable profitability level. We have therefore decided to exit our personal banking operations and are considering various options. We will honour our obligations to service our current customer base, and the exit could therefore last for several years. The number of branches and the headcount will be reduced. From 1 January 2015, the personal banking activities will be presented as Non-core operations, Danske Bank said.

The Latvian branch of Danske Bank became part of the Danish Danske Bank Group in 2007. At the end of September 2014, the Latvian branch of Danske Bank ranked 15th among the banks operating in Latvia in terms of assets.

Danske Bank has operations also in Estonia and Lithuania.

Riga newsroom, +371 6708 8606, eko_zinas@ bns.lv

HD Danske Bank to close six offices in Estonia
WC 227 words
PD 3 February 2015
ET 09:49
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Baltic News Service

LP 

TALLINN, Feb 03, BNS Danske Bank plans to close six offices in Estonia and cut back staff accordingly during this year to focus on private and corporate banking in the future.

The bank will offer an outplacement program to all leaving employees. The offices will be closed gradually with consideration of customer relations and client service aspects. Customers will be notified of the closings well in advance to ensure smooth transfer of service to other offices. As regards nonresident customers, the bank's Estonian unit will in the future focus more on international clients with business interests in the Baltic states, it appears from the bank's annual report.

TD 

In the segment of personal banking, Danske Bank will focus on serving private banking customers to support offers targeting corporate customers. The bank expects growth in both customer segments but has no growth targets for retail banking in 2015.

The Estonian unit of Danske Bank plans to invest close to 15 million euros over the next two years, including investment in creating a uniform Baltic IT platform integrated into the group's platform.

Danske Bank earned a net profit of 22.7 million euros in Estonia last year. A year earlier it netted 47.3 million euros.

Tallinn newsroom, +372 610 8823, majandus@bns.ee

SE Finance
HD Danske shrinks losses to 201m
BY Fiona Reddan
WC 223 words
PD 4 February 2015
SN The Irish Times
SC IRTI
PG 3
LA English
CY (c) 2015, The Irish Times.

LP 

Danske Bank shrunk its Irish losses before tax to 201.5 million in 2014, down from 241 million the previous year, as loan impairments fell by 29 per cent.

Denmark's biggest bank, which announced its full-year results on Tuesday, continued its retrenchment in the Irish market in 2014, making "considerable headway" with the winding-up of its non-core Irish operations.

TD 

Total lending fell from DKK 53.7 billion (7.2 billion) to DKK 37.5billion (5 billion), and all transaction accounts were closed. After the first half of 2015, only the personal mortgage portfolio will remain on its books, the bank said.

Danske Bank operated a personal and business banking franchise in Ireland, first under the National Irish Bank brand, then its own.

Downsizing operations

It is currently downsizing its Irish operations by quitting retail banking with a view to focusing on servicing larger corporations.

The figures show that 101 people were employed by the bank in Ireland at the end of 2014.

"In the past 18 months, we have successfully refocused our business in Ireland and are now concentrating our efforts on leveraging our technology and advisory expertise to deliver a superior service to corporate and institutional clients," said Terry Browne, head of corporate and institutional banking at Danske Bank Ireland.

HD Danske Bank Lithuania's gross profit in 2014 at EUR 10.42mn
WC 584 words
PD 4 February 2015
SN Lithuanian News Agency - ELTA
SC ELTA
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Lithuanian News Agency - ELTA

LP 

Vilnius, February 4 (ELTA) - The gross profit of the Lithuanian subsidiary of the largest Danish group of financial services Danske Bank A/S last year was LTL 36 million (EUR 10.42 million), the branch said in an annual report.

In 2014, the extensions to decrease bad debts were reduced by LTL 2 million (EUR 0.58 million); in 2013 these extensions were reduced by LTL 63 million (EUR 18.25 million). Small changes in extensions in 2014 show the stability of loan portfolio, national economics and financial situation of bank's clients.

TD 

Compared to the year 2013, last year the net income from interest of Danske Bank increased by 3 percent. It was mostly determined by diminishing expenditure of insurance and loan financing. When the country was approaching the time when it had to join common euro zone, the volumes of deposits grew especially rapidly in the last months of last year and increased by 30 percent, in comparison to deposit portfolio of the end of 2013. The net income from commission increased by 6 percent because of higher activeness of the bank's clients: the extent of payment transactions grew up and payment by cards was getting more active.

"Last year was especially important for the domestic banking sector and for the State on the whole. Business was preparing especially actively to join common currency of euro zone. It is probable that as Lithuania became the 19th country of euro zone, it will induce higher interest of foreign investors in our market," says Gintautas Galvanauskas, managing director of Danske Bank in Lithuania.

According to the data of survey on servicing quality of the bank's clients conducted by the company of market researches Dive during the last quarter of the year 2014, Danske Bank became the bank that services the clients the best in Lithuania. It is for the third time during the last four years already that the bank received such an award.

"We always try to provide our business clients with the highest value. Following the renewed strategy of Danske Bank in the Baltic States, this year we are going to focus even more on the services to the companies and we will increase our activeness in this segment. We have set an ambitious goal for the year 2015 - to increase the portfolio of business clients up to 10 percent," Galvanauskas. According to him, the major attention will be given to the clients of private banking and clients in high need of complex banking services.

The bank plans to invest EUR 15 million into its subsidiaries ank in the Baltic States in the next 1-2 years. The part of these investments will be meant to create common IT platform and to synchronise it with the systems of the entire group. The growing concentration on the business clients and improved services will secure profitable growth in the future. Meanwhile, with regard to retail banking sector, it is predicted that more and more transactions of retail banking clients will be carried out online using the e-channels offered by the bank.

This year the bank will continue expanding the servicing centre of Danske Bank Group that has been working in Lithuania for several years already, and the newly established IT centre of Danske Bank. These centres already have more than 650 employees and it is planned to increase their number by several hundred within the upcoming years.

Irma Janiauskait

HD Bank of Ireland(Governor&Co) Acquisition of Commercial Loan Portfolio
WC 1264 words
PD 5 February 2015
ET 05:30
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright 2015, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

TIDMBKIR

RNS Number : 1428E

TD 

Bank of Ireland(Governor&Co)

05 February 2015

The Governor and Company of the Bank of Ireland ('Bank of Ireland')

Acquisition of Performing Commercial Loan Portfolio

___________________________________________________________________________

Bank of Ireland and Goldman Sachs have agreed terms to acquire a commercial loan portfolio of face value EUR540m from Danske Bank A/S. As part of the transaction, Bank of Ireland will acquire a EUR274m portfolio of performing commercial loans, comprising over 1,000 customers in the SME, Agriculture and CRE sectors. Goldman Sachs in conjunction with Pepper Asset Servicing, as servicer, will acquire the balance of the portfolio. The transaction is expected to close shortly.

Mr Mark Cunningham, Director of Bank of Ireland Business Banking commented "Bank of Ireland is pleased to have been able to avail of this opportunity to demonstrate our ongoing focus on further growing and developing our strong position in serving the business and agri sectors in Ireland. We look forward to welcoming these new customers to Bank of Ireland and working with them as they seek to develop and grow their own businesses and enterprises".

the potential exposure of the Group to various types of market risks, such as interest rate risk, foreign exchange rate risk, credit risk and commodity price risk; deterioration in the credit quality of the Group's borrowers and counterparties, as well as increased difficulties in relation to the recoverability of loans and other amounts due from such borrowers and counterparties, have resulted in significant increases, and could result in further significant increases, in the Group's impaired loans and impairment provisions; implications of the Personal Insolvency Act 2012 and measures introduced by the Central Bank of Ireland to address mortgage arrears on the Group's distressed debt recovery and impairment provisions; the impact on lending and other activity arising from the emerging macro prudential policies; the performance and volatility of international capital markets; the effects of the Irish Government's stockholding in the Group (through the Ireland Strategic Investment Fund) and possible changes in the level of such stockholding; the impact of downgrades in the Group's or the Irish Government's credit ratings or outlook; the stability of the Eurozone; changes in the Irish and United Kingdom banking systems; changes in applicable laws, regulations and taxes in jurisdictions in which the Group operates particularly banking regulation by the Irish and United Kingdom Governments together with implementation of the Single Supervisory Mechanism and establishment of the Single Resolution Mechanism; the exercise by regulators of powers of regulation and oversight in Ireland and the United Kingdom; the introduction of new government policies or the amendment of existing policies in Ireland or the United Kingdom; the outcome of any legal claims brought against the Group by third parties or legal or regulatory proceedings or any Irish banking inquiry more generally, that may have implications for the Group; the development and implementation of the Group's strategy, including the Group's ability to achieve net interest margin increases and cost reductions; the responsibility of the Group for contributing to compensation schemes in respect of banks and other authorised financial services firms in Ireland and the United Kingdom that may be unable to meet their obligations to customers; the inherent risk within the Group's life assurance business involving claims, as well as market conditions generally; potential further contributions to the Group sponsored pension schemes if the value of pension fund assets is not sufficient to cover potential obligations; the exposure of the Group to NAMA losses in the event that NAMA has an underlying loss at the conclusion of its operations, which could adversely impact the Group's capital and results of operations; the impact of the continuing implementation of significant regulatory developments such as Basel III, Capital Requirements Directive (CRD) IV, Solvency II and the Recovery and Resolution Directive; and the Group's ability to address weaknesses or failures in its internal processes and procedures including information technology issues and equipment failures and other operational risks.

HD *Bank Of Ireland Buys Comml Loan Portfolio
WC 188 words
PD 5 February 2015
ET 05:30
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright 2015, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

5 Feb 2015 05:30 ET *Bank Of Ireland Buys EUR274M Performing Comml Loan Portfolio

5 Feb 2015 05:51 ET Bank Of Ireland, Goldman Sachs to Buy Commercial Loan Portfolio from Danske Bank

TD 

By Razak Musah Baba

LONDON--Bank of Ireland and Goldman Sachs have agreed terms to acquire a commercial loan portfolio worth 540 million euros ($605 million) in face value from Danske Bank A/S.

As part of the transaction, Bank of Ireland will acquire a EUR274 million portfolio of performing commercial loans, comprising over 1,000 customers in the small and medium enterprises, or SME, agriculture and commercial real estate, or CRE, sectors.

Goldman Sachs together with loan servicing firm Pepper Asset Servicing, will acquire the balance of the portfolio. The transaction is expected to close shortly.

Bank of Ireland, Ireland's largest bank, is still 14% owned by the Irish government after receiving a bailout during the financial crisis.

-Write to Razak Musah Baba at razak.baba@wsj.com; Twitter: @Raztweet

HD TRLPC-BoI and GS to acquire 540 mln euro loan portfolio from Danske
BY By Claire Ruckin
WC 216 words
PD 5 February 2015
ET 09:02
SN Reuters News
SC LBA
LA English
CY Copyright 2015 Thomson Reuters. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

LONDON, Feb 5 (Reuters) - Bank of Ireland and Goldman Sachs have agreed to acquire a portfolio of Irish commercial loans with a face value of 540 million euros ($617 million) from Danske Bank, Bank of Ireland announced on Thursday.

Bank of Ireland will acquire 274 million euros of performing Irish commercial loans consisting of over 1,000 customers in the SME, agricultural and commercial real estate sectors, while Goldman Sachs will acquire 266 million euros of loans.

TD 

Danske decided to sell the portfolio of non-core loans, called Project Griffin Loan Portfolio Sale, as part of a continued wind down of its non-core division, Danske Bank Ireland, Danske said in a statement.

Goldman has mandated asset management firm Pepper Asset Servicing in Ireland to service the portfolio on the bank's behalf.

Both banks will acquire the portfolios via their balance sheets and the transaction is expected to close in the second quarter of 2015.

Banks have had renewed appetite to put balance sheets to work and grow loan books to increase incomes on higher yielding assets with lower default risks, banking sources said. ($1 = 0.8752 euros) (Editing by Christopher Mangham)

HD Press Release: Danske Capital Selects Sustainalytics as Its ESG Research and Data Provider
WC 531 words
PD 9 February 2015
ET 02:30
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright 2015, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

TD 

 
   Firm Plans to Integrate Sustainalytics' ESG Insights Into Its Investment 
Products 
 
   AMSTERDAM, Netherlands, Feb. 9, 2015 (GLOBE NEWSWIRE) -- Sustainalytics 
http://www.globenewswire.com/newsroom/ctr?d=10119090&l=1&a=Sustainalytics&u=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.sustainalytics.com%2F[http://www.globenewswire.com/newsroom/ctr?d=10119090&l=1&a=Sustainalytics&u=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.sustainalytics.com%2F] 
, a leading provider of environmental, social and governance (ESG) 
research and analysis, has been selected by Danske Capital, an 
international asset manager and part of the Danske Bank Group, to 
provide a comprehensive suite of ESG research and data solutions that 
will be integrated into the manager's investment products. 
 
   "Our firm understands and embraces the importance of carefully 
considering and monitoring ESG factors, so we wanted to work with a 
leading provider whose core business is built on a very strong 
responsible investing foundation," said Robert Mikkelstrup, Senior Vice 
President at Danske Capital. "By making Sustainalytics' ESG research and 
ratings available to our own portfolio managers and analysts, Danske 
Capital can facilitate a more holistic, thoughtful approach to 
investing." 
 
   Headquartered in Denmark with more than EUR100bn in assets under 
management worldwide, Danske Capital focuses in-house resources on the 
management of Nordic, European and Eastern European assets, where their 
market knowledge, resources and systems are in the best position to 
deliver excellent performance for clients, while working with external 
managers that offer expertise in other regional markets around the 
world. 
 
   Going beyond a standard subscription agreement, Danske Capital and 
Sustainalytics plan to work together this year to advance the dialogue 
around responsible investing best practices, helping investors better 
understand ESG integration. 
 
   "We are honored to have been selected by Danske Capital to help their 
portfolio teams integrate ESG factors into their solutions-based 
approach to investing," said Sustainalytics' Chief Executive Officer, 
Michael Jantzi. "We look forward to working with Danske to bring a 
higher level of understanding around ESG-related risk to the global 
investment community." 
 
   About Sustainalytics 
 
   Headquartered in Amsterdam, Sustainalytics is an independent ESG 
research and analysis firm supporting investors around the world with 
the development and implementation of responsible investment strategies. 
With 13 offices globally, Sustainalytics partners with institutional 
investors who integrate environmental, social and governance information 
and assessments into their investment decisions. Today, the firm has 
over 200 staff members, including more than 100 analysts with varied 
multidisciplinary expertise of more than 40 industries. For the past 
three years, Sustainalytics was voted best independent responsible 
investment research firm in Extel's IRRI survey. For more information, 
visit www.sustainalytics.com[http://www.sustainalytics.com].

HD Danske Bank reduces Lithuania's GDP growth estimate to 2.5 pct
WC 641 words
PD 11 February 2015
SN Lithuanian News Agency - ELTA
SC ELTA
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Lithuanian News Agency - ELTA

LP 

Vilnius, February 11 (ELTA) - According to the calculations carried out by Danske Bank, falling import in Russia will cost Lithuanian economy EUR 0.5 billion in nominal value in 2015, i.e. more than projected earlier. Therefore, Danske Bank has reduced Lithuania's GDP growth estimate from 2.7 to 2.5 percent. In 2016 GDP growth should return to 3.1 percent, the latter estimate has not been changed.

Latvian and Estonian GDP growth projections have also been reviewed. Latvia's GDP growth rate is forecast at 2.6 percent in 2015 (previous estimate 2.9 pct) and 3.1 percent in 2016. Estonia's economy will grow by 2.2 percent in 2015 (previous estimate 2.3 percent) and by 2.7 percent in 2016.

TD 

Danske Bank analysts say that Lithuania's economy will lose EUR 0.5 billion due to the Russian effect. In December 2014 Lithuania's export to Russia decreased by 18 percent, whereas in 2015 it is projected to fall by 25 percent.

In 2015 exporters will face problems not only because of the falling rouble but also because the actual Russian economy will experience a deep recession. Consumption and investment is lagging in Russia due to high interest rate, reaching 15 percent, and an increase of imported goods prices by 30-50 percent. Thus, in 2015 consumption in Russia is projected to decrease by 5.5 percent while investments by 12 percent. Russia's economy is expected to fall by 8 percent in 2015 and by another 1 percent in 2016. As a result, import volume is expected to drop by 30 percent in 2015 and by another 4 percent in 2016.

Danske Bank Analyst of the Baltic States Rokas Grajauskas says that the reduction of import in Russia will undoubtedly affect Lithuania and other countries that are dependent on the Russian market. In 2014 Russia was Lithuania's main export partner outside the EU. Nonetheless, despite the Russian sanctions on food products, export of goods and services to Russia grew by 4 percent to reach EUR 6.2 billion or 21 percent of the aggregate Lithuania's export.

Danske Bank projects that this year Lithuania's export losses to Russia will amount to EUR 1.5 billion, i.e. export of goods and services should shrink by 25 percent in 2015 and by another 3 percent in 2016.

Lithuanian traders that are engaged in re-export of investment goods to Russia, such as manufacturing machinery or technical equipment will feel dire consequences. Lithuanian transport and tourism sectors have already felt the effects of lagging Russian economy for some time now. The situation will be exacerbated not only by the slowing Russian economy or falling rouble but Russian sanctions on the import of agricultural and food products.

On the other hand, what will facilitate the situation is the fact that 88 percent of goods exported to Russia are re-exported goods. They have a lower added value for the Lithuanian economy compared to goods of Lithuanian origin. What will help withstand the impact is the fact that the euro has appreciated against the rouble significantly less than the dollar did, as well as the fact that most of Lithuanian origin goods exported to Russia are consumer goods and not investment goods.

The analyst has ascertained that there is also goods news. For example, despite of losses in Russia, Lithuania's total export in 2015 should grow by 1 percent, due to recovering economy of the euro area and new markets. Lithuanian businesses for which the Russian market closed have shifted to other markets. They have successfully increased sales not only in the euro area countries but in lesser known markets such as the United States, Saudi Arabia and Southeast Asia.

Karolis Broga

HD Danske to charge some clients as Danish negative rates trickle through
WC 276 words
PD 13 February 2015
ET 07:27
SN Reuters News
SC LBA
LA English
CY Copyright 2015 Thomson Reuters. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

COPENHAGEN, Feb 13 (Reuters) - The impact of negative interest rates in Denmark has started to trickle through to the real economy as Danske Bank announced on Friday that several thousand of its business clients would now have to pay to deposit their cash.

The country's largest bank said it would negotiate individual rates with the wealthiest of its business clients although did not say who the clients could be, what rates they would pay and from when.

TD 

"Typically, this is more professional customers with bigger deposits that we'll make individual agreements with," Danske Bank head of press relations Kenni Leth said, adding that 4 percent of the bank's business clients would be affected.

The central bank has slashed rates an unprecedented four times in four weeks to -0.5 percent, effectively charging commercial banks to park their money with it.

Chief Executive Thomas Bergen raised the prospects of charging some clients for deposits during an earnings call last week, although he said Danske would try to avoid doing that with ordinary customers.

"We really want to avoid that. That would be too much for me and for society," he told a conference call.

Leth reiterated that sentiment but added the bank was "following the market closely and will act accordingly".

FIH Erhversbank, a smaller Danish Bank, said last week both of its retail and business clients would have to pay a rate of 0.5 percent on their regular accounts as of March 2015. (Reporting by Alexander Tange; Editing by Sabina Zawadzki and Mark Potter)

HD *S&P Affirms Realkredit Danmark's Cov Bonds; Outlook Stable
WC 2051 words
PD 20 February 2015
ET 11:48
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright 2015, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

20 Feb 2015 11:48 ET Press Release: S&P Affirms Realkredit Danmark's Cov Bonds; Outlook Stable

TD 

 
 
The following is a press release from Standard & Poor's: 
 
OVERVIEW 
     -- We have reviewed our ratings on Realkredit Danmark's General Capital 
Center mortgage covered bond program under our revised covered bonds criteria 
published on Dec. 9, 2014. 
     -- Following our review, we have affirmed our ratings on the covered bond 
program and related issuances. 
     -- The stable outlook on our rating on the General Capital Center 
reflects our view that adverse movements in the long-term ICR on the parent 
Danske Bank would not automatically trigger a change to our ratings. 
 
LONDON (Standard & Poor's) Feb. 20, 2015--Standard & Poor's Ratings Services 
said today that it has completed its review of its ratings on Danish issuer 
Realkredit Danmark A/S' General Capital Center mortgage covered bond program 
by applying its revised criteria for rating covered bonds (see "Covered Bonds 
Criteria" and "Methodology And Assumptions For Assessing Portfolios Of 
International Public Sector And Other Debt Obligations Backing Covered Bonds 
And Structured Finance Securities," both published Dec. 9, 2014, on 
RatingsDirect). As a result, we have affirmed at 'AAA' our ratings on the 
covered bond program and related issuances. The outlook is stable. 
 
On publishing our revised criteria, we had placed our ratings on those covered 
bond programs that could be affected by a published change in criteria "under 
criteria observation" (see "Covered Bond Program And Spanish Multicedulas 
Ratings Placed Under Criteria Observation," published Jan. 12, 2015). 
Following our review, we have removed our "under criteria observation" 
identifier from the ratings on the covered bonds issued from Realkredit 
Danmark's General Capital Center. 
 
Under our covered bonds criteria, we organize the analytical process for 
rating covered bonds into four key stages: 
     -- Performing an initial analysis of issuer-specific factors--legal and 
regulatory risks and operational and administrative risks--which mainly assess 
whether a rating on the covered bond may be higher than the rating on the 
issuer. 
     -- Assessing the starting point for the rating analysis, based on the 
applicable resolution regimes, to determine the reference rating level (RRL). 
     -- Determining the maximum achievable covered bond rating from an 
analysis of jurisdictional and cover pool-specific factors. 
     -- Combining the results of the above and incorporating any additional 
factors, such as counterparty risk and country risk, to assign the final 
covered bond rating. 
 
After assessing the RRL, to determine a maximum achievable covered bond rating 
we analyze jurisdictional and collateral support. Our assessment of the 
expected jurisdictional support for mortgage covered bond programs in Denmark 
is "very strong" (see "Assessments For Jurisdictional Support According To Our 
Covered Bond Criteria," published Dec. 22, 2014). Under our covered bonds 
criteria, the uplift from the RRL can be up to three notches when the 
jurisdictional support is assessed as "very strong". Under our analysis of 
jurisdictional support, we determine a jurisdiction-supported rating level 
(JRL), which is our assessment of the creditworthiness of a covered bond 
program once we have considered the level of jurisdictional support, but 
before giving credit to the amount of collateral. We give no benefit to 
jurisdictional support in our analysis (that is, zero incremental uplift for 
jurisdictional support), where the RRL is already at or above the level of the 
sovereign rating. In this case, the JRL is the same as the RRL. 
 
Following the assessment of the RRL and JRL, we analyze the credit quality of 
the cover pool and the availability of liquidity support and committed 
overcollateralization to determine the maximum collateral uplift. 
 
When applicable, we cap our ratings on mortgage covered bond programs under 
our updated criteria for rating single-jurisdiction securitizations above the 
sovereign foreign currency rating (RAS criteria). Given the current ratings on 
Denmark (AAA/Stable/A-1+), the maximum rating on the program is AAA (see 
"Methodology And Assumptions For Ratings Above The 
Sovereign--Single-Jurisdiction Structured Finance," published Sept. 19, 2014). 
 
Lastly, the ratings on the program and related issuances are not constrained 
by legal, operational, or counterparty risks. 
 
We are affirming our issue rating on the program at 'AAA'. The 'AAA' rating 
reflects our RRL of 'a' and JRL of 'aa' for the program, as well as four 
notches of uplift for collateral support, which is reduced to three after 
accounting for voluntary OC commitment. The stable outlook on our rating on 
the General Capital Center reflects our view that adverse movements in the 
long-term issuer credit rating (ICR) on Danske Bank (parent company) would not 
automatically trigger a change to our ratings. 
 
POTENTIAL EFFECTS OF UPCOMING CRITERIA CHANGES 
Our ratings are based on our current applicable criteria, including those set 
out in the criteria article "Covered Bond Ratings Framework: Methodology And 
Assumptions," published on June 26, 2012. Please note that we have published a 
proposal on the analysis for commercial real estate "Request For Comment: 
Methodology And Assumptions: Analyzing European Commercial Real Estate 
Collateral In European Covered Bonds," published on Dec. 11, 2014. 
 
As a result of this review, our future criteria applicable to rating covered 
bonds, which include commercial real estate assets, may differ from our 
current criteria. These criteria changes may affect the ratings on the 
outstanding covered bonds issued by Realkredit Danmark. Until such time that 
we adopt new criteria, we will continue to rate and surveil these covered 
bonds using our existing criteria (see the list of related criteria and 
research below). 
 
RELATED CRITERIA AND RESEARCH

9, 2014 
     -- Covered Bonds Criteria, Dec. 9, 2014 
     -- Methodology And Assumptions For Ratings Above The 
Sovereign--Single-Jurisdiction Structured Finance, Sept. 19, 2014 
     -- Europe Asset Isolation And Special-Purpose Entity Criteria--Structured

     -- Covered Bond Ratings Framework: Methodology And Assumptions, June 26,

HD Maersk 2014 Net Profit Below Forecasts; Sells Danske Bank Stake
BY By Ian Walker
WC 386 words
PD 25 February 2015
ET 02:55
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright 2015, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

Danish conglomerate A.P. Moeller-Maersk A/S (MAERSK-A.KO) on Wednesday reported a net profit of $5.02 billion for 2014, slightly below market expectations, and said it is selling its 20.05% interest in Danske Bank A/S (DANSKE.KO) for $5.5 billion.

The firm, which employs over 88,900 people and is present in over 130 countries, added that it will return the money raised from the sale of its interest in Danske Bank to shareholders. It will decide the exact value ahead of its annual general meeting in March.

TD 

Net profit for the year rose to $5.02 billion, compared with $3.45 billion in 2013, on revenue of $47.57 billion and $47.39 billion respectively. It had forecast net profit for the year of $5.8 billion.

Underlying profit, which excludes discontinued operations, impairments and divestment gains, was in line with its expectations at $4.53 billion, compared with $3.41 billion in 2014. The company had forecast an underlying profit of $4.5 billion.

For 2015, Maersk expects to report underlying profit below 2014, excluding Danske Bank. Gross cash flow used for capital expenditure will be around $9 billion in 2015, compared with $8.7 billion in 2014.

Maersk Line, the world's biggest container-shipping company in terms of capacity, has booked an impairment loss of $2.2 billion for Maersk Oil

Maersk has declared a dividend of 300 Danish kroner ($45.57).

-Write to Ian Walker at ian.walker@wsj.com; @IanWalk40289749

Corrections and Amplifications

This item was corrected at 08:20 GMT. The original incorrectly said the profit was below the company's forecast.

25 Feb 2015 03:19 ET Correction to Maersk 2014 Earnings Story

Danish conglomerate A.P. "Maersk 2014 Net Profit Below Forecasts; Sells Danske Bank Stake," at 0740 GMT, incorrectly said the profit was below the company's forecast.

HD Maersk posts 2014 result in line, to sell Danske Bank stake
WC 141 words
PD 25 February 2015
ET 02:28
SN Reuters News
SC LBA
LA English
CY Copyright 2015 Thomson Reuters. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

COPENHAGEN, Feb 25 (Reuters) - Danish shipping and oil group A.P. Moller-Maersk booked $2.2 billion in impairment losses at its oil unit on Wednesday and said it would sell its 20 percent stake in Danske Bank, Denmark's largest bank.

It said it would sell the majority of its Danske Bank stake to the Maersk family foundation, which controls the company, and the proceeds, expected to amount to around $5.5 billion, would be spent as dividends for shareholders.

TD 

The largest container shipping company in the world posted 2014 results broadly in line with expectations in a Reuters poll, with net revenues at $47.57 billion and net profit of $5.2 billion. (Reporting by Ole Mikkelsen; Editing by Balazs Koranyi)

HD Maersk to sell its 20% stake in Danske Bank
BY Richard Milne, Nordic Correspondent
WC 516 words
PD 25 February 2015
ET 05:32
SN Financial Times (FT.Com)
SC FTCMA
LA English
CY Copyright 2015 The Financial Times Ltd. All rights reserved. Please do not cut and paste FT articles and redistribute by email or post to the web.

LP 

AP Mller-Maersk has bowed to investor pressure as the Danish shipping-to-oil conglomerate said it would sell its 20 per cent stake in the country's biggest bank.

Shareholders can expect a special dividend of up to $5.5bn, the value of Maersk's holding in Danske Bank. But most of the 20 per cent stake in Danske will remain in familiar hands as the family foundation behind Maersk will buy the majority of the shares.

TD 

Maersk's chairman, Michael Pram Rasmussen, said: "Over a period we have been met with requests from shareholders to divest our shares in Danske Bank . . . Such a sale is now possible and will at the same time secure a long-term Danish ownership of Danske Bank. In addition AP Mller-Mrsk can focus resources on its activities within shipping and oil."

The stake sale is the latest in a series of disposals and portfolio adjustments at Maersk, Denmark's biggest company by revenues, since Nils Andersen took over as chief executive seven years ago.

Mr Andersen sold Maersk's supermarket business a year ago for $3bn and initiated its first share buyback programme. The former Carlsberg chief executive has tried to focus the once sprawling conglomerate on four main areas: container shipping, oil production and exploration, port terminals, and drilling rigs.

That strategy led to mixed results on Wednesday when Maersk also reported its full-year earnings.

Maersk Line, the world's biggest container shipping line, continued its strong performance by boosting net profit to $2.3bn last year from $1.5bn in 2013.

But Maersk Oil, once the main profit contributor of the group, suffered from the falling oil price, resulting in big writedowns and swinging from a $1bn profit to a $861m net loss. On an underlying basis, Maersk said its oil division only had slightly lower profits at $1bn.

Maersk Line, seen as a bellwether for global trade as it transports 15 per cent of all seaborne freight, said it expected container demand to grow 3-5 per cent this year, well below the pre-crisis levels of more than 10 per cent. It also expects to post a higher underlying profit this year than in 2014. Maersk as a whole said it expected an underlying profit this year if slightly below $4bn, compared with $4.1bn in 2014.

Maersk has been a big Danske shareholder since 1928. AP Mller Holding, a family company that is Maersk's biggest owner, has offered to buy 15 per cent of Danske from the conglomerate and indicated its intention to buy an additional 2.02 per cent. Maersk shareholders will also be offered some Danske shares.

Ane Uggla, chairman of A.P Mller Holding, said: "By acquiring shares in Danske Bank we reinforce the historic relations which have existed since the late 1920s . . . In doing so we wish to preserve Danske Bank's close and longstanding ties to Denmark and provide our support to the positive development in both AP Mller-Maersk and Danske Bank."

HD Takeover of Danske Bank is a no-go after Maersk deal - analysts
BY By Ole Mikkelsen
WC 471 words
PD 25 February 2015
ET 09:29
SN Reuters News
SC LBA
LA English
CY Copyright 2015 Thomson Reuters. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

COPENHAGEN, Feb 25 (Reuters) - The acquisition of a stake in Danske Bank by the family behind the A.P. Moller-Maersk conglomerate will likely bar any takeover attempts of Denmark's largest bank, as had been previously rumoured.

Maersk said on Wednesday it would sell its 20 percent stake in Danske, with a holding company controlled by the family-run A.P. Moller Foundation taking 15 percent.

TD 

"It is to ensure the long-term ownership of Danske Bank and ensure the bank's roots in the Danish society," Ane Maersk McKinney Uggla, chairman of the foundation, told Reuters.

"With the acquisition ... we maintain the historic links that have existed since the late 1920s," the media-shy chairman said.

Maersk founder Arnold Peter Moller stepped in to rescue Danske Bank in the 1920s, becoming its chairman, and relations have been tight since, with the two companies sharing board members for decades.

The note of economic nationalism in Uggla's comments is nothing new -- Maersk created its oil unit Maersk Oil in 1962 only when it became apparent that German companies were interested in developing newly found oil in the Danish sector of the North Sea.

Danske Bank used to be the Nordic region's largest financial institution until the financial crisis that played out after 2008, when it was hit hard by a Danish housing slump and ill-timed acquisitions in Ireland, which needed an EU bailout.

Since then rumours of a takeover of a weakened Danske have recurred with Sweden's SEB being touted as a potential suitor.

"Rumours of possible mergers involving Danske Bank can be put aside for now," Nordea Markets analyst Christian Hede said.

The 15 percent stake in Danske Bank will be owned by A.P. Moller Holding, controlled by the foundation. A.P. Moller Holding controls 41.51 percent of A.P. Moller-Maersk's shares but 51.09 percent of the voting rights.

Uggla is the daughter of Maersk McKinney Moller who headed the group as CEO from 1965 until 1993 although he continued as a dominant chairman until 2003 and even after that the group sought his consent on major decisions.

He died in 2012, aged 98.

In its 110-year history the group grew into a conglomerate with activities far away from shipping but since Moller's death, CEO Nils Andersen has pledged to shed non-core assets and focus on the five units that constitute its shipping and oil business.

Analysts say up next on the block could be Maersk's 38.75 percent stake in car transporter Hoegh Autoliners, airliner Star Air as well as logistics company Damco. (Reporting by Ole Mikkelsen; editing by Sabina Zawadzki and Terje Solsvik)

HD 42% fall in financial complaints
WC 217 words
PD 25 February 2015
SN RTE.ie
SC RTEI
LA English
CY Copyright 2015. RTE

LP 

There were just under 4,500 complaints to the office of the Financial Services Ombudsman in 2014, a fall of 42% from the year before.

Almost half of these resulted in some form of redress for those customers with complaints against financial services companies.

TD 

The Ombudsman said that new powers given to the office last year - meaning the complaints upheld against individual financial services providers can be published - had a significant effect on complaint handling by the industry.

It said this means that more complaints are being dealt with at an earlier stage, and settled, and that this is a very positive outcome for the industry.

Danske Bank Group and credit card firm Avant Tarjeta, or Avant Card, had the most complaints substantiated and partly substantiated by the office.

The majority of complaints in 2014 were about investment products, but this sector also saw the biggest reduction in complaints, down by 65%.

Complaints about insurers fell by 49% and complaints against banks were 27% lower.

On a product basis, mortgages continue to be the highest driver of complaints, representing 28% of all complaints received.

The Ombudsman said mortgage issues remain a concern and more work needs to be done.

Compensation paid out last year rose by 2.4% to almost 950,000.

26 Feb 2015 08:07 ET Danske Bank: Public Prosecutor Drops Price Manipulation Case

TD 

   By Dominic Chopping

Denmark's Danske Bank A/S (DANSKE.KO) said Thursday that the Danish Public Prosecutor for Serious Economic and International Crime (SOIK) has dropped the case against the bank that had accused it of price manipulation.

The case was brought against Danske Bank, Realkredit Danmark and six employees on 7 February 2014 but all accusations have now been dropped, it said.

HD Russia's economy may contract by around 5.5 pct in 2015 - Danske Bank Lithuania
WC 293 words
PD 26 February 2015
SN Lithuanian News Agency - ELTA
SC ELTA
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Lithuanian News Agency - ELTA

LP 

Vilnius, February 26 (ELTA) - Chief analyst of Danske Bank Lithuania Branch Rokas Grajauskas says that Russia's economy is forecast to contract by around 5.5 percent this year. The tendency is first of all determined by the depreciation of the rouble due to falling oil prices. The embargo imposed by Russia on goods from the European Union and sanctions applied by the United States led to a significant increase of import prices and consumption decline.

Grajauskas was one of the speakers at the 7th Economy Conference of Lithuania. According to him, the actions of Russia's Central Bank also had an effect on the declining economy. In the last quarter of 2014 it spent USD 42 billion in the foreign currency market trying to save the rouble. However this and the drastic increase of interest rates had no effect on the rouble's depreciation. On the contrary, it led to a panic in Russia's financial market.

TD 

The economist said that the crisis in Russia significantly affected Lithuania's export to Russia and in 2015 it is projected to shrink by 25 percent. The economist noted that Lithuanian businesses are flexibly shifting to other markets. Lithuania's businesses managed to compensate for 43 percent of losses suffered in the Russian market, mostly by increasing export to Belarus by 20 percent, Germany by 8 percent, the Saudi Arabia by 4 percent, the United States by 3 percent and Italy by 2 percent.

At the 7th Economy Conference of Lithuania reports are delivered by heads of banks, financial or state institutions and major enterprises, as well as the leading experts and well known journalists writing on economy.

Karolis Broga

SE Shipping
HD Maersk to hand $6.6 B to investors after selling Danske bank stake
WC 583 words
PD 27 February 2015
SN Manila Bulletin
SC MABULL
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Manila Bulletin Publishing Corp. All rights reserved.

LP 

Copenhagen - Danish shipping and oil group A.P. Moller-Maersk will hand shareholders a $6.6 billion windfall in dividends this year after it sells its 20 percent stake in Denmark's biggest bank Danske.

Analysts had expected Maersk to announce the divestment of some assets on Wednesday as part of its strategy of focusing on its core shipping and oil divisions - but the Danske Bank stake had not been among the anticipated sales.

TD 

Maersk - the world's largest container shipping company - said it would sell 15 percent to its controlling shareholder, the Moller family foundation, saying the deal ensured Danske remained in Danish hands and had a long-term major investor.

[caption id="attachment_245450" align="alignright" width="300"] WORLD'S BIGGEST CONTAINER SHIP - The MV Maersk Mc-Kinney Moller, the world's biggest container ship, arrives at the harbor of Rotterdam in this August 16, 2013 file photo. Danish shipping and oil group A.P. Moller-Maersk said it would sell its 20 percent stake in Danske Bank with the anticipated proceeds of about $5.5 billion going to shareholders. The world's largest container shipping company said the family foundation that controls the company has committed to buying 15 percent of the country's largest bank and that the sale to the foundation ensures that Danske Bank remains Danish.[/caption]

It will offer the remaining 5 percent to other existing Maersk shareholders, it added.

The conglomerate did not specify how much the foundation was paying for the 15 percent Danske stake, but said it would correspond to $5.5 billion.

That $5.5 billion will go to shareholders at about 1,569 crowns a share, Maersk said, and it also proposed dividends of $1.1 billion for the 2014 business year, or 300 a share.

Maersk's shares jumped by more than 8 percent to top 15,000 crowns, close to a record high of 15,070 crowns hit last September after Maersk announced its first share buyback programme and analysts upgraded their price targets.

You'll have a more streamlined conglomerate as an investment case, said Alm. Brand analyst Jesper Christensen.

They no longer have capital stashed in a bank and this will be looked upon positively, especially for the many foreign investors - for example from the US - thinking 'I want to invest in shipping, so why should I invest in a Danish bank?'.

Ana Uggle, the granddaughter of Maersk's founder and head of the foundation, told Reuters: It is to ensure the long-term ownership of Danske Bank and ensure the bank's roots in Danish society.

In recent years, Maersk has sold off assets such as stakes in supermarkets and Danish shipping company DFDS as well as fleets of Liquefied Natural Gas (LNG) and crude oil tankers and oil production vessels.

The Danske stake sell is immensely positive and will help reduce a discount on Maersk shares that exists because the company is a conglomerate, said Jesper Langmack, head of equity investments at PFA, a pension fund that is the largest Maersk shareholder aside from the foundation that controls it.

If they judge that it's non-core for their business, then I think its reasonable enough (that they continue selling non-core assets), but they've already sold off a lot of non-core, so they're close to their goal. There's not much non-core left, he told Reuters.

Dnipropetrovsk, February 27 (Interfax-Ukraine) The EU is allocating EUR 1.5 million to Dnipropetrovsk region to provide aid to displaced persons from Crimea and Donbas, the press service of Dnipropetrovsk Regional Administration has reported.

The agreement between the EU and Dnipropetrovsk Regional Administration was signed on Thursday.

TD 

The funds will be used to repair, restore and furnish 15 facilities in seven towns in Dnipropetrovsk region. Over 2,000 of most vulnerable persons - women, children and the elderly will be accommodated there between one and a half to two months.

The project will be realized by the Dopomoha Dnipra charitable foundation with the support of Dnipropetrovsk Regional Administration.

Over 87,000 displaced persons from Crimea, Donetsk and Luhansk regions currently live in Dnipropetrovsk region.

Kyiv, February 27 (Interfax-Ukraine) The National Bank of Ukraine (NBU) on February 26 decided to liquidate the insolvent banks BG Bank and Legbank (both based in Kyiv), reads a post on the NBU's website.

"Shareholders and top managers of the above-mentioned banks did not take measures aimed at preventing insolvency of the banks on time, in particular, they did not remove a lack of liquidity and did not fulfill liabilities to depositors and creditors on time," reads the report.

The central bank said that BG Bank and Legbank were put on the list of insolvent banks under NBU resolutions No. 744 and 745 of November 27, 2014. Temporary administration at the banks expired on February 27, 2015.

Legbank was founded in 1989, and BG Bank in 1994.

BG Bank ranked 84th among 158 operating banks as of January 1, 2015, in terms of total assets worth UAH 1.301 billion, and Legbank ranked 133rd with UAH 396 million, according to the National Bank of Ukraine.

Kyiv, February 27 (Interfax-Ukraine) Remittances to Ukraine totaled $3.885 billion in equivalent in 2014, while remittances abroad amounted to $644.6 million, reads a post on the National Bank of Ukraine (NBU) website.

The NBU said that as of early 2015, 26 money transfer systems, including 20 created by banks, were operating in Ukraine.

A total of 20 international money transfer systems created by nonresidents were functioning.

As reported, remittances to Ukraine in 2013 reached $4.084 billion.

Kyiv, February 27 (Interfax-Ukraine) - Real wages in Ukraine (excluding Crimea and Sevastopol) in January 2015 fell by 17.3% from January 2014 and they fell by 16.7% from December 2014, the State Statistics Service has said.

The fall in real wages in January 2015 year-over-year was seen in Luhansk region (32.7%), Poltava region (19.5%), Kharkiv region (19.3%), Zhytomyr region (19%), Kyiv and Chernihiv regions (18.8% each), Kirovohrad and Kherson regions (17.9% each), Rivne region (17.8%), Ivano-Frankivsk and Chernivtsi regions (17.7% each), Volyn region (17.5%), Cherkasy region (17.4%), Sumy region (17%), Khmelnytsky and Ternopil regions (16.2% each), Zaporizhia region (16%) and Kyiv City (15.7%).

The State Statistics Service said that the average wages of full-time employees in Ukraine in January 2015 fell from December 2014 was 13.9% down and grew by 9.1% compared to January 2014 to UAH 3,455 against UAH 4,920 in December, UAH 3,534 in November and UAH 3,509 in October.

In December 2014 the highest rate of wages of full-time employees was registered in Kyiv, where it was UAH 5,385, while Ternopil region saw the lowest wage being UAH 2,403.

Kyiv, February 27 (Interfax-Ukraine) - The total sum of wage arrears in Ukraine in January 2015 saw an 11% rise, the State Statistics Service has reported.

According to the State Statistics Service, wage arrears on February 1, 2015 amounted to UAH 1.466 billion, or 5.1% of the monthly wage fund for January.

As of February 1, 2015, the wage arrears of economically active enterprises, establishments, and organizations totaled UAH 994.465 million, those of economically inactive entities UAH 154.504 million; and the debts of bankrupt enterprises were UAH 316.633 million.

As the report reads, in January 2015 wage arrears Luhansk region grew by 40.3%, to UAH 87.896 million, while in Donetsk region it fell by 3.2%, to UAH 352.143 million. The growth of wage arrears was observed in Volyn region (87.5%), Chernivtsi region (27.4%), Sumy region (27.1%), Vinnytsia (25.4%), Dnipropetrovsk (25.4%), Cherkasy (21.7%) and Lviv region (20.1%).

In the past month, wage arrears declined in Zakarpattia (11.9%), Zhytomyr (9.8%), Ivano-Frankivsk (7.4%) regions and Kyiv city (4%).

Over the past month, the total amount of debt in industry increased to UAH 930.824 million (17.9%), furniture and other products production, vehicle and equipment repair to UAH 27.492 million (81.1%), production of vehicles and equipment to UAH 84.771 million (79.9%), mining and quarry development to UAH 261.311 million (46%), production of key pharmaceutical products to UAH 529 million (38.1%) and crude oil refining to UAH 12.308 million (20.1%).

The total amount of debt in production of wooden, paper products and printing decreased by 24.3%, to UAH 9.37 million, it fell in production of chemicals to UAH 34.589 million (8.6%) and production of foods, beverages and tobacco to UAH 25.267 million (6.2%).
