Simferopol, February 27 (Interfax) - The Crimean authorities have nationalized some 250 private facilities and no new decisions on nationalization will be made, Sergei Aksyonov, the head of the Republic of Crimea, said.

"There are some 250 private facilities. An overwhelming majority of them are property of [Ukrainian businessman Ihor] Kolomoisky, and the money for it will go to depositors [of Kolomoisky-controlled PrivatBank, which stopped working in Crimea after the region's reunion with Russia]," Aksyonov told reporters in Simferopol on Friday.

The parliament of Crimea on Friday made a number of decisions on the nationalization of private property and a decision to stop the nationalization mechanism.

"We are now ending the nationalization process. This decision is the last one," Sergei Aksyonov, the head of the Republic of Crimea, said in the parliament.

Aksyonov also said the facilities nationalized by the Crimean State Council on Friday were previously privatized with violations of the law.

"We are talking primarily about those facilities that were fraudulently removed from state property. Those facilities were not just privatized in a non-transparent manner, they were stolen form the state,' Aksyonov said.

"The list of property registered as property of the Republic of Crimea is final and new objects will not be included in it after March 1, 2015, the Crimean parliament said in its decision.

Simferopol, February 27 (Interfax) The State Council of Crimea on Friday decided to stop the mechanism of private property nationalization on March 1, an Interfax correspondent has reported.

"The list of property registered as property of the Republic of Crimea is final and new objects will not be included in it after March 1, 2015, the Crimean parliament said in its decision.

INDUSTRY

Kyiv, February 27 (Interfax-Ukraine) - Public joint-stock company Zaporizhtransformator (ZTR), a large global manufacturer of transformer equipment, has delivered four 300 MVA 500 kV transformers to the Argentinean port of Zarate within the agreed deadline, ZTR said in a press release on Thursday.

The transformers will be supplied to the El Bracho, Henderson, Rosario Oeste and Colonia Elia substations.

Argentina's leading transmitting company Transener S.A. and interstate Argentinean-Uruguayan energy company CTM Salto Grande bought the equipment.

The transformers were bought under a state investment energy program on improving the Argentinean energy sector. The total cost of the program is ARS 900 million.

ZTR's rivals in the tender were ABB (Brazil), Siemens (Brazil) and Hyosung (South Korea).

ZTR, part of Energy Standard Group belonging to businessman Konstantin Grigorishin, supplies goods to 86 countries. It produces power oil transformers, power reactors, and controlled shunt reactors.

FUEL & ENERGY COMPLEX

Krasnoyarsk, February 27 (Interfax) Russia's Energy Ministry has confirmed its participation in trilateral gas negotiations between Russia, Ukraine and the European Commission that will be held in Brussels on March 2, Energy Minister Alexander Novak told reporters at the Krasnoyarsk Economic Forum.

"We agreed that I will come on Monday. We agreed with the European commissioner that we will hold trilateral consultations. This will be in Brussels," Novak said.

He expects that the implementation of the trilateral agreement that was signed in October 2014 will be discussed at the trilateral meeting.

"First of all we will talk about the situation concerning supplies of current gas to Ukraine and transit of gas to European consumers, in other words the implementation of the agreements that were stipulated in the trilateral agreements of October 31 in Brussels. Since the winter package has not ended yet, March is still ahead," Novak said.

A spokesman for the EC told Interfax on Thursday evening that the EC had received confirmation from the Russian Energy Ministry that Russia would participate in the trilateral meeting on gas supplies with the European Union and Ukraine in Brussels on March 2.

The meeting will be held in the afternoon, and there is no briefing or press conference planned, he said, adding that the press would probably informed with a final statement.

Krasnoyarsk, February 27 (Interfax) Russia might discuss gas shipments to Donbas at talks in Brussels on March 2, Energy Minister Alexander Novak told journalists on Friday.

"I confirmed my participation [in the talks on March 2]. In Brussels, we're planning to discuss the entire spectrum of our relations, mostly how the Brussels agreements are being carried out. On Monday we'll consult with the European Commission and our Ukrainian partners. The agenda concerns solely the winter package," he said.

"I think that this topic [gas shipments to Donbas] will certainly be touched upon," he added.

Kyiv, February 27 (Interfax) Ukraine's national oil and gas company Naftogaz Ukrainy has transferred Gazprom $15 million in prepayment for shipments of Russian gas in March, Naftogaz CEO Andrei Kobolev told journalists on Friday.

He said that this advance corresponded to around 50 million cubic meters of gas.

Kobolev added that Ukraine had not yet used 120 million cubic meters of gas it previously paid Gazprom for.

According to the Brussels agreements, the state holding has the right to prepay at any point in time, he said.

Concerning future payments for additional volumes of Russian gas in March, Kobolev said: "That will depend on the weather, which affects things tremendously, as well as on shipments from Europe and how much we'll be able to increase [them]. We are even planning for a certain increase in March."

In addition, gas supplies from Hungary are expected to grow, he said. Around 5.8 million cubic meters are imported each day, but this can be increased to 14-16 million cubic meters. In addition, it is possible that the throughput capacity of gas shipments to Ukraine through Slovakia will grow to 45 million cubic meters from 41 million in March.

He also said that Gazprom confirmed its readiness not to count gas shipped to the ATO zone in the contract with Naftogaz.

Kobolev also noted that a halt in Russian gas shipments to Ukraine does not threaten its transit to Europe. Ukraine has already demonstrated its reliability as a transporter, he said.

Moscow, February 27 (Interfax) Gazprom has received a $15 million payment from Ukraine's national oil and gas company Naftogaz Ukrainy, but this amount is only enough for a day's worth of gas, Gazprom's official representative Sergei Kupriyanov told journalists.

"Today at 9:20 a.m. Gazprom received a $15 million payment from Naftogaz Ukrainy. At the currently level of shipments, this prepayment is enough for only about one day," he said.

Energy Minister Alexander Novak told journalists that Naftogaz's prepayment was enough for gas until Tuesday. "If Naftogaz paid for another day, that means there are enough paid resources to last until Tuesday, including Monday; that is, the deadline when prepaid gas runs out is moved by a day if they paid $15 million," he said.

Novak added that the current contract envisions Russia cutting off gas shipments if prepayment is not made. He said this was one of the terms of the contract that was signed.

Moscow, February 27 (Interfax) - Ukraine's national oil and gas company Naftogaz Ukrainy and consumers in Donbas will receive 68.9 million cubic meters of Russian gas on Friday, Gazprom's official representative Sergei Kupriyanov told journalists.

"The overall amount of shipments to Ukraine today will be 68.9 million cubic meters, and all Naftogaz Ukrainy requests will be fulfilled for the points of entry they specified," he added.

Krasnoyarsk, February 27 (Interfax) Gazprom may shut off gas supplies to Ukraine if payment is not received by the end of the day on Monday, Energy Minister Alexander Novak told journalists.

"If Gazprom does not receive the money by the end of the day on Monday, the situation arises when gas supplies may be shut off effective on Tuesday," Novak said.

The $15 million that Gazprom received from Naftogaz Ukrainy on Friday are sufficient for just one day's worth of supplies, he said.

Gas for customers in Europe will continue being supplied in full, he said.

Krasnoyarsk, February 27 (Interfax) - Ukraine needs to buy around 2 billion cubic meters (bcm) of gas from Russia by the end of the heating season, Energy Minister Alexander Novak told Interfax.

"According to estimates from the gas industry, Ukraine still needs to buy at least up to 2 bcm of gas from Russia by the end of the autumn-winter period," he said.

"The end of the autumn-winter season is actually the end of March," Novak added.

Krasnoyarsk, February 27 (Interfax) Russia and the EU are worried about gas transit if shipments to Ukraine stop, Energy Minister Alexander Novak told Interfax.

"This likelihood exists, certainly," he said.

"This possibility was discussed back in the summer. We met specially to agree on getting rid of these transit risks. Really, given that Ukraine is not in fact carrying out our Brussels agreements on paying for gas and shipping using the prepayment method, we and the EU currently see such risks. For that reason, work is now underway on getting Ukraine to prepay for future gas shipments as soon as possible," Novak added.

Kyiv, February 27 (Interfax-Ukraine) Russia suspending gas supplies to Ukraine won't threaten gas transit to Europe, Naftogaz Ukrainy CEO Andriy Kobolev told journalists in Kyiv on Friday.

He said that Ukraine had demonstrated its reliability as a transit partner several times.

Kobolev also said that it had particularly demonstrated its reliability in summer-spring 2014, when Ukraine didn't purchase Russian gas but had shipped gas to Europe in full volume.

Kyiv, February 27 (Interfax-Ukraine) Board Chairman of national joint-stock company Naftogaz Ukrainy Yaroslav Klymovych and Director of Baker Hughes for Eastern Europe Lukasz Ostrowski on February 24 discussed cooperation in oil and gas extraction, the press service of the Ukrainian company has reported.

Representatives of Baker Hughes initiated the meeting due to the expansion of its operations in Eastern Europe.

According to the report, a representative of Baker Hughes said that the company is ready to jointly develop plans on possible cooperation with Ukrainian extracting companies on introducing exploration, drilling and fossil fuel transportation technologies

Klymovych said that the proposal on cooperation will be discussed at the state level.

"The top priority task for us is the development of the Ukrainian energy market, and this partnership would be able to promote the fulfillment of the task," he said.

As reported, in February 2015 Nadra Ukrainy signed a memorandum of cooperation in exploration drilling with Poland's EXALO Drilling S.A.

Nadra Ukrainy was established in October 2000 to improve the efficiency of state geological exploration enterprises. The state owns 100% of the company.

A top-tier oilfield service company, Baker Hughes provides solutions that help oil and gas operators make the most of their reservoirs. With 60,000 employees in more than 80 countries, the company's local geo-market teams work side by side with customers to engineer reliable, application-specific products and services.

Kyiv, February 27 (Interfax-Ukraine) - Ukraine decreased gas production by 0.4% or by 7.5 million cubic meters on the continental part of the country in January 2015 year-on-year, to 1.675 billion cubic meters (bcm), including a 0.04% decrease or 700,000 cubic meters to 1.62 bcm of natural gas, a source at Ukrainian Energy and Coal Industry Ministry has told Interfax-Ukraine.

Naftogaz's enterprises, not taking into account Chornomornaftogaz, cut gas production by 2.6% or 37.5 million cubic meters, to 1.406 bcm, including 1.36 bcm of natural gas, down 2.3% or 31.3 million cubic meters.

Naftogaz unit Ukrgazvydobuvannia cut gas production by 1.7%, to 1.269 bcm, of which 1.259 bcm of natural gas, down 1.2%, and Ukrnafta reduced it by 10.2%, to 137.1 million cubic meters, including 100.1 million cubic meters of natural gas, down 14.2%.

Other oil and gas companies operating in Ukraine raised output by 12.6% or 30 million cubic meters, to 268.4 million cubic meters of gas, including 260.9 million cubic meters of natural gas, up 13.3% or 30.7 million cubic meters.

Among large gas producers last month were also PrJSC Nafotgazvydobuvannia with 87.03 million cubic meters (59.8% up year-on-year), ESKO-Pivnich LLC energy services company with 51.81 million cubic meters (10% down), KUB-Gas LLC with 22.329 million cubic meters (13.7% down), PrJSC Natural Resources with 17.983 million cubic meters (25.4% down), PrJSC Ukrnaftoburinnia with 14.369 million cubic meters (17.2% up), First Ukrainian Petroleum Company with 12.803 million cubic meters (70.3 times up), JV Poltava Petroleum Company with 11.462 million (34.1% down), PrJSC Ukrgazvydobutok with 9.873 million (2.9% down), Sirius 1 Ltd. with 7.433 million cubic meters (3.1% down), Nadra-Geoinvest with 4.884 million cubic meters (100% up), Regal Petroleum with 4.801 million (5.9% down), CJSC Davon with 3.582 million cubic meters (4.4% down), private JSC Tisagaz with 2.871 million cubic meters (18.3% up), Sakhalynske LLC with 2.784 million cubic meters (18.8% down), LLC BET (Pari) with 2.775 million cubic meters (61% up), PrJSC Plast with 2.425 million cubic meters (38.8% down), UkrCarpatOil JV with 2.306 million cubic meters (7.1% down), Prom-Energo-Product Ltd. with 1.523 million cubic meters (9.4% down), PKF Dion LLC with 1.366 million cubic meters (4.4% down), Boryslav Petroleum Company with 904,000 cubic meters (9.3% up), Nadragaz LLC with 857,000 cubic meters (44.3% up), Nadra Ukrainy with 807,000 cubic meters (23.2% up), Eastern Geology Union LLC with 766,000 cubic meters (45.9% down), Delta JV with 412,000 cubic meters (1.2% up) and Kashtan Petroleum Ltd. with 248,000 cubic meters (10.5% down).

As reported, gas production in Ukraine in 2014 increased by 1.9% (excluding Crimea), to 20.17 billion cubic meters.

Kyiv, February 27 (Interfax-Ukraine) Ukraine cut natural gas consumption by 14.5% or 561.6 million cubic meters in the period from February 1 to February 20, 2015, to 3.307 billion cubic meters (bcm), the press service of national joint-stock company Naftogaz Ukrainy reported on Thursday.

The limits set for industrial companies, heat supply companies and budget-funded organizations for the period were exceeded by 11.4%: with the target of 1.614 bcm the said companies and organizations consumed 1.797 bcm of gas.

The press service said that industry consumed 814.7 million cubic meters of gas with the target of 766.7 million cubic meters), heat supply companies 911.1 million cubic meters (758 million cubic meters) and budget-funded organizations 71.6 million cubic meters (89.3 million cubic meters).

Industrial companies over the period increased gas consumption by 3% year-over-year, which could be linked to full functioning of Rivneazot and Cherkasy Azot.

Households consumed 1.509 bcm of gas in the period with the target of 1.876 bcm.

Kyiv, February 27 (Interfax-Ukraine) National Nuclear Generating Company Energoatom plans to raise credit lines with the limits of UAH 400 million and UAH 300 million (multicurrency) from Oschadbank and a credit line of $40 million from Alfa-Bank (both based in Kyiv).

According to the Energoatom's announcement in the Visnyk Derzhavnykh Zakupivel state procurements bulletin, the three lines were accepted on February 18, 2015.

The UAH 400 million credit line will be opened at 24% per annum in hryvnias, the UAH 300 million credit line at 24% per annum in hryvnias or 13% per annum in the U.S. dollars and the $40 million credit line at 13.75% per annum in the U.S. dollars.

The funds will be raised for one year.

Energoatom operates 15 nuclear power blocks, equipped with VVER reactors, with combined capacity to generate 13.835 gigawatts.

Minsk, February 27 (Interfax-Ukraine) Belarus is ready to supply electricity to Ukraine, Belarusian Energy Minister Vladimir Potupchik said at a press conference in Minsk on Thursday.

"We're ready to propose to Ukraine that we supply electricity to their market," he said, adding that the initiative was suggested by Ukraine.

The minister said that Belarus plans to double electricity exports in 2015.

He also said that Belarus plans to import 2.5 billion kilowatt-hours (kWh) of electricity from Russia in 2015.

In 2014, Belarus did not supply electricity to Ukraine, but bought Ukrainian electricity instead. Contracts on the supply of electricity from Ukraine expired in November 2014. From October 2014 Ukraine decided to halt its export of electricity, including to Belarus.

Kyiv, February 27 (Interfax) The self-proclaimed Luhansk People's Republic (LPR) has disconnected from power supply from Ukraine and has fully switched to power supply from Russia, the administration of the Luhansk region of Ukraine has reported.

"The self-proclaimed republic is taking all electrical power from the Russian Federation," Hennadiy Moskal, the head of the Luhansk region's administration, said.

Moskal reiterated that the LPR "had fully disconnected from power supply from Ukraine" as of Friday.

"That is, the thermal electrical power plant in Schastia and the thermal electrical power plant in Severodonetsk are not supplying a single kilowatt to the occupied territories," Moskal said on the official page of the Luhansk region's state administration on Facebook on Friday morning.

AGRO-INDUSTRIAL COMPLEX

Kyiv, February 27 (Interfax-Ukraine) Majority shareholder in Sweden's Agrokultura AB with assets in Ukraine and Russia applied for delisting of its shares from NASDAQ First North in Stockholm, according to a company report on its website.

Salermo S.A. and Magna Finance Investments Limited (earlier Magna Investments Limited) holding 94.4% of shares in the company initiated an extraordinary general meeting of shareholders for February 26, 2015.

The shareholders planned to change of company category from public limited liability company to private limited liability company.

It was proposed that the board would consist of three directors for the time until the end of the next annual general meeting. Vladimir Kuznetsov is elected as a new director of the board until the end of the next annual general meeting. Werner Kuester and Simon Hallqvist would resign from the board and leave their seats for disposal in connection with the meeting.

Salermo S.A. and Magna Finance Investment Limited also initiated a compulsory redemption of the shares. There have not been legal conditions to initiate a compulsory redemption of the outstanding shares in Agrokultura.

Salermo S.A. and Magna intend to assemble their holding of shares in Agrokultura so that there will be legal conditions to initiate a compulsory redemption of the outstanding shares in Agrokultura. The compulsory redemption of the outstanding shares in Agrokultura is expected to be initiated shortly after the last day of trading in Agrokulturas shares (February 27, 2015).

Swedish agricultural company Agrokultura (earlier Alpcot Agro) was registered in 2006.

In 2013, Agrokultura saw net loss rise by 2.6 times compared to 2012, to SEK262 million. Its revenues amid falling prices for agricultural products declined by 8%, to SEK617 million.

In summer 2014, Steenord Ltd. investment company (the British Virgin Islands) increased its stake in the charter capital of the Swedish agricultural company with assets in Ukraine and Russia Agrokultura AB to 47%. The company indicated that Steenord is controlled by Russian businessman of Ukrainian origin Nikolay Fartushnyak - the co-founder and co-owner of the Sportmaster retail chain. In August Agrokultura also announced its new major shareholder nominated its representative Achim Lukas to its board of directors.

Kyiv, February 27 (Interfax-Ukraine) The Lauffer Group has said that a ban on flour exports will not stop the rise in price of flour on the Ukrainian market.

"The ban on exporting flour will not be a hindering factor on price growth. The Ukrainian flour market does not face a shortage of flour, it has always seen extra amounts of flour," the company's press service told Interfax-Ukraine.

Lauffer Group said that the problem for bakeries is not in a shortage of flour but its high price.

"The prices of grain products are mainly formed thanks to the expenses of farmers who depend on the forex rates (fuel, lubricants, fertilizers, machinery, etc.). With the ban on exporting flour the problem would not be resolved. Moreover the flour milling sector will be under the threat of destruction," the company said.

The group said that the company is cooperating with reliable suppliers of raw materials who fulfill their liabilities.

As reported, bakeries are preparing an address to the Cabinet of Ministers of Ukraine asking that the flour exports be banned to avoid a further increase in the price of bread.

A meeting of producers, the Agricultural Policy and Food Ministry and the Agrarian Fund was also held. The Agrarian Fund said that it will create a simplified trading system through the Agrarian Exchange for bread producers and plans to launch the system in the near future.

SERVICES

Moscow, February 27 (Interfax) The Russian Foreign Ministry said Russian citizens going to Ukraine will need foreign travel passports to enter and leave the country from March 1.

"The Russian Foreign Ministry is pointing out to Russian citizens going to Ukraine that, in accordance with a decision made unilaterally by the current Ukrainian administration, transit, stay and travel on the territory of Ukraine will not be possible with Russian passports (internal passports) and children's birth certificates (for children under the age of 14) stating their Russian citizenship," the Russian Foreign Ministry said in a report.

Russian citizens can use the following documents to enter, leave stay in and travel on the territory of Ukraine: a foreign travel passport, a diplomatic passport, a service passport, seaman's identity card, entry (return) certificate to Russia (only for return to Russia), and a flight certificate of an aircraft crewmember.

Kyiv, February 27 (Interfax) The Ukrainian National Council on Television and Radio Broadcasting has decided that Russia's Mir 24 television does not meet the requirements of he Ukrainian legislation and the European Convention on Transfrontier Television, the regulator said on Facebook on Thursday.

The decision was made based on the results of the monitoring of the channel conducted on February 13, 19 and 20. The monitoring registered news reports and fragments of television programs containing "calls for a change of the constitutional system in Ukraine, advertisement of the Russian peacekeeping forces, propaganda of war and violation of the territorial integrity of Ukraine."

Kyiv, February 27 (Interfax-Ukraine) State financing of the state program on reforming and developing the utilities sector for 2010-2014 in Ukraine reached UA 4.6 billion or 20% of the target, and the realization of a currently unapproved, similar program would be impossible without state support and private investors, First Deputy CEO of the Association of Cities of Ukraine, former first deputy head of Kyiv City Administration and ex-deputy regional development, construction, housing and utilities economy minister Oleksandr Mazurchak said at the Ukrainian Forum of Infrastructure Development (UFID) 2015 in Kyiv on Thursday.

"It was planned that the state was to earmark UAH 26 billion for the reforms. The funds were not allocated. Maybe only one fifth of the funds were sent to the purpose," he said, adding that the state had not supported the reforms with funds, laws, organizations and the media, and that the reforms had actually failed.

Mazurchak said that a new state program has been drawn up, but not adopted. He said that the reformation of the utilities sector is only possible with state support, the introduction of public private partnership, the protection of investors as a key source of reform financing and the protection of the interests of poor people in light of the increase in utilities tariffs.

TELECOMS & TRANSPORT SECTORs

Moscow/Kyiv, February 27 (Interfax-Ukraine) Russia's OJSC Mobile Telesystems (MTS) has transferred 100% of its shares in private joint-stock company MTS Ukraine to indirect ownership, reads a report issued by the Russian company.

From February 26, 2015, 100% of MTS Ukraine now belongs to Dutch Preludium B.V., owned by Luxemburg's Allegretto Holding.

"The asset was transferred to expand the opportunities of raising investment in MTS Ukraine," MTS Spokesperson Elena Kokhanovskaya told Interfax.

MTS Ukraine's press service has told Interfax-Ukraine that the change to European jurisdiction will facilitating dialog with potential investors and attract them towards participating in joint investment projects.

In October 2014, telecommunications market sources said that MTS is looking for a foreign partner for joint investment in the building of a 3G communications network in Ukraine.

MTS Ukraine won a 3G communication license at an auction held on February 23, 2015. The company will pay UAH 2.72 billion (around $100 million). Another two licenses were bought by Kyivstar (subsidiary of Russia's Vimpelcom Ltd.) and Astelit (55% belongs to Turkcell and 45% to Rinat Akhmetov's SCM).

Simferopol, February 27 (Interfax) The parliament of Crimea has nationalized the property of the Ukrainian mobile communications operator Kyivstar in the region, Sergei Aksyonov, the head of the Republic of Crimea, said.

"They did not re-register as a Russian enterprise, they did not pay people wages, and the property was abandoned," Aksyonov told reporters on Friday, responding to a question from Interfax following the meeting of the Crimean state Council where the decision on the nationalization was made.

Kyiv, February 27 (Interfax-Ukraine) The largest Ukrainian mining and metal company Metinvest plans to lease Berdiansk airport (Zaporizhia region) to transport its foreign specialists to Mariupol (Donetsk region) where two of its largest metal companies are located Mariupol Illich Steel Works and Azovstal.

The company sent its proposal to Berdiansk Town Council. It was planned to discuss the leasing of the airport by Metinvest at a Thursday session of the council, however the issue was removed from the agenda.

Metinvest confirmed to Interfax-Ukraine that the company is still interested in leasing the airport.

"Despite the fact that the runway of the air field is in bad condition, Metinvest is ready to restore it to launch charter flights to carry specialists (including from Europe) to Mariupol. Specialists are needed to realize investment projects at Mariupol steel works," the company said.

Metinvest is a vertically integrated group of mining companies that manages assets in every link of the production chain, from iron ore and coke production to semi-finished and finished steel products and rolled metal piping, as well as the production of other goods with high added value.

CONSTRUCTION & REAL ESTATE

Kyiv, February 27 (Interfax-Ukraine) The Confederation of Constructors of Ukraine (CCU) plans to ask both the government and the parliament to ensure state financing for affordable housing programs in 2015, in the amount of around UAH 500 million.

The decision to prepare an address to the government and profile parliamentary committees was made by the CCU Board at a meeting on February 25 in Kyiv.

The confederation said that the above-mentioned sum foresees the realization of existing and new state housing programs.

This concerns plans to realize the state affordable housing program for military servicemen and participants of the anti-terrorist operation (ATO) in eastern Ukraine.

Due to inflation and the devaluation of the hryvnia the CCU Board decided to address the relevant parliamentary committees on revising the cost of one square meter for constructors who participate in the state programs and fix prices for certain dates.

LAW

Moscow, February 27 (Interfax) Both conflicting sides in Ukraine have been observing the Minsk agreements, for instance, they have been withdrawing heavy armaments from the frontline, deputy chief monitor of the OSCE Special Monitoring Mission to Ukraine (OSCE SMM) Alexander Hug said.

The OSCE "welcomes that both sides are now indicating that they are taking steps to comply with these responsibilities," he said in an interview with the RT television channel.

"The OSCE requiresnot only the starting point where the hardware is located; it also requires the routes and most importantly the storage places the hardware will go to in the end," Hug said.

While commenting on the additional demands posed by the OSCE, Hug stated: "We are not putting up demands, the demands are clear. What we are tasked by the Minsk arrangement and by our mandate is to go out and monitor what the parties do."

Eduard Basurin of the Defense Ministry of the self-proclaimed Donetsk People's Republic (DPR), said earlier that the militants started to withdraw its weapons at 10 a.m. on Thursday in the presence of OSCE monitors. He added that five OSCE teams were operating on the ground.

Kyiv also reported beginning the withdrawal of heavy armaments from the Debaltseve area in the Donetsk region and the Donetsk airport amongst other locations on Thursday. Deputy head of the Ukrainian Interior Ministry's department in the Donetsk region Illia Kiva said that the withdrawal would continue along the entire line of contact if the militia honored their commitments.

Kyiv, February 27 (Interfax) Ukrainian President Petro Poroshenko said the Ukrainian troops are ready to return heavy weapons to their previous locations in Donbas if the enemy violates the Minsk agreements.

"Our military are ready to return the hardware to its previous locations at any time, at any moment and stand up to the enemy within the shortest period," Poroshenko said at a graduation ceremony in the Ukrainian Defense Ministry's Cherniakhovsky National University on Friday.

Kyiv, February 27 (Interfax-Ukraine) Even if a long lasting peace is established in eastern Ukraine, there will still be a military threat to the country, Ukrainian President Petro Poroshenko has said.

"In the case of the most optimistic scenario in Donbas, in the case of a long-lasting ceasefire which could bring forward a political settlement and stable peace, unfortunately, a military threat from the east will still exist and will require constant efforts and the strengthening of the defense capacity of the state," Poroshenko said, during a graduation ceremony at the Ukrainian Defense Ministry's Cherniakhovsky National University on Friday.

Moscow, February 27 (Interfax) Russian Foreign Minister Sergei Lavrov has called on Ukraine to maintain its non-aligned status in order to prevent the country's split.

"Kyiv needs to keep its non-aligned status in order to prevent Ukraine's split and maintain the atmosphere of trust and stability in the Euro-Atlantic region," he told teachers and students of the Russian Foreign Ministry's Diplomatic Academy on Friday.

Moscow, February 27 (Interfax) Trucks of the Russian Emergency Situations Ministry carrying humanitarian aid to Ukraine's south-eastern regions have already arrived at the border and are currently undergoing customs clearance, the deputy director of the ministry's National Crisis Management Center, Oleg Voronov, has said.

"During its journey, the convoy of the Russian Emergency Situations Ministry split in two. Some of the trucks arrived at the Donetsk border crossing point, and the others at Matveyev-Kurgan, where their cargo is now undergoing customs clearance," he said.

Ukrainian customs officers are inspecting the Russian supplies at two checkpoints. They have not made any complaints. Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe (OSCE) observers are monitoring the procedure. Journalists are also present at the border crossing points.

More than 80 trucks will soon leave the Donetsk checkpoint and head to the Luhansk region, while the same number of vehicles will arrive in the city of Donetsk from the Matveyev-Kurgan checkpoint.

The Russian convoy is carrying over 1,800 tonnes of humanitarian aid, mostly food, including canned meat and fish, condensed milk, semolina, rice, buckwheat and sugar. The cargo also includes first necessity items, as well as books and educational aids for school and university students of Donbas.

It is the 16th humanitarian aid convoy sent by Russia to the south-east of Ukraine since August 2014.

Kyiv, February 27 (Interfax) Ukrainian Interior Minister Arsen Avakov has announced the opening of a criminal investigation into Thursday's clash between police and protesters outside the National Bank building in Kyiv.

"I ordered an investigation into those events. Its results will be made public no later than in 48 hours. A commission headed by two deputy interior ministers Eka Zguladze and Serhiy Yarovy will work. As for my negotiations with protesters near the National Bank last night, we agreed that demonstrators would provide photo-, video- and other materials in order to ensure an impartial inquiry. A criminal case was opened into the clashes," Avakov wrote on Facebook.

"Following a prompt inquiry immediately after the events, I decided to dismiss the head of Kyiv's Pechersky district police department and suspend his deputy for public security pending conclusions of the investigative commission," he said.

"The country's gold and forex reserves are stored at the National Bank building. Any destabilization around this building creates a huge risk of destabilization on a national scale," the Ukrainian interior minister said.

Avakov promised to ask the National Bank governor and Ukraine's ministers in charge of economic issues to resolve the problem that triggered the February 26 protest.

The minister called on people who attended the action to "behave appropriately."

Avakov also apologized for "the unprofessional conduct of police during that situation and the disgusting scene near the National Bank building."

Kyiv, February 27 (Interfax) Officers of law enforcement agencies did not use physical force against people attending a protest outside the Ukrainian National Bank building in Kyiv, the Interior Ministry's branch for the city said in a press release on Friday.

"A group of citizens were holding a protest near the National Bank of Ukraine at around 9:00 p.m. The protesters were using construction pallets to build a fence. They also brought barrels and car tires to the National Bank building. Municipal workers arrived at the action venue. They tried to dismantle the tents, barricades and other reinforcements installed on the pavement. As a result, clashes erupted between Kyiv residents, municipal workers and protesters. Soldiers of the National Guard of Ukraine separated the people in order to prevent further unlawful actions," it said.

"The municipal services then received an opportunity to do their job. They removed the barricades and took them out of the city center. Meanwhile, two citizens called an ambulance to the National Bank building and said that they had been injured during the dispute," it said.

"Police are verifying this information. Law enforcers themselves did not use physical force against the sides in the conflict," according to the press release.

Kyiv, February 27 (Interfax) Kyiv police officers have tried to disperse a picket near the National Bank without authorization by the Ukrainian interior minister or any other official, according to Yuriy Lutsenko, head of the Petro Poroshenko Bloc's parliament group.

"Any use of force against citizens is impermissible. If anyone has used force against them, the perpetrators and, most importantly, those who gave that order will be punished," Lutsenko said in the Pravo na Vladu talk show aired by the 1+1 television channel early on Friday morning.

"Whenever people have many reasons to protest and the authorities make too many mistakes, they have the right to peaceful assembly, to pickets and to utterances," Lutsenko said.

Krasnoyarsk, February 27 (Interfax) - The Russian government is planning to consider changing wheat export duties in the middle of March, Deputy Prime Minister Arkady Dvorkovich said at an economic forum in Krasnoyarsk.

"The decision will come after February. In about 10 days we're going to consider the results of February completely and we'll discuss it then," he told journalists when asked if the government was planning to change the export duties on wheat.

Leverkusen, February 27 (Interfax) - German chemical and pharmaceutical concern Bayer boosted sales in Russia 17% to 742 million euro in 2014, senior Bayer representative in Russia and CIS Vera Hahn said in an interview with Interfax.

The Bayer HealthCare pharmaceutical division increased sales 20% to 531 million euro and sales of the Bayer CropScience agricultural divisions rose 23% to 95 million euro.

However, the Bayer MaterialScience division, which produces high-tech polymer materials, saw sales decline 4% to 116 million euro, reflecting a slowdown in such sectors as automotive manufacturing and industrial construction, Hahn said.

HD Danish pension funds pool $150 mln for business loans
WC 159 words
PD 2 March 2015
ET 06:18
SN Reuters News
SC LBA
LA English
CY Copyright 2015 Thomson Reuters. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

COPENHAGEN, March 2 (Reuters) - Danish pension funds ATP, Danica Pension and PensionDanmark are pooling 1 billion Danish crowns ($150.36 million) in a new fund that will provide loans for the country's small and medium sized businesses.

The three also invited other pension funds to participate in the venture, expected to be operational before summer, top Danish fund ATP said in a statement Monday.

TD 

The target group for the new fund is businesses with a yearly turnover above 50 million crowns and borrowing needs above 10 million.

"The fund gives small and medium sized Danish businesses access to responsible loan capital, and it gives us access to an interesting investment opportunity. We believe the investment can give ATP members a decent return," CEO Carsten Stendevad said in the statement. ($1 = 6.6506 Danish crowns) (Reporting by Alexander Tange, editing by Terje Solsvik)

HD Danske Bank: Lithuania approaching deflation record
WC 233 words
PD 10 March 2015
ET 07:12
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Baltic News Service

LP 

VILNIUS, Mar 10, BNS - Lithuania, which in February recorded a 1.8-percent annual deflation based on national standards, has come close to the deflation record set early in 2003 when the consumer prices fell by an annual 2 percent, Danske Bank has said on Tuesday.

Prices for energy resources remain the key factor chiefly responsible for driving down the prices Another reason was the onset of harsh price competition between major retail centers, Rokas Grajauskas, a Baltic analyst at the bank, said in a press release.

TD 

Meanwhile, the annual growth in services' prices continued to accelerate. In January, prices for services rose by an annual 2.6 percent and in February, by 3.1 percent, he said.

The growth of services' prices is mainly being driven by the growth of household income Prices for most services are not affected by international trade factors and the dynamics of services prices provides a better reflection of the growth of consumption spending than the dynamics of goods prices. Moreover, prices for energy resources have a lesser impact on services prices, the analyst said.

Stronger acceleration in inflation is expected by the bank at the end of the year. As estimated by Danske Bank, the inflation rate should increase to 1.5 percent in the final months of 2015.

Vilnius newsroom, verslas@bns.lt, +370 5 205 8520

HD In second half of 2015 negative inflation is expected become positive - Danske Bank Lithuania
WC 278 words
PD 10 March 2015
SN Lithuanian News Agency - ELTA
SC ELTA
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Lithuanian News Agency - ELTA

LP 

Vilnius, March 10 (ELTA) - Deflation of prices has reached all time record in Lithuania. Negative inflation levels were only greater in early 2003 when the yearly decrease of prices reached 2 percent.

Analysts of Danske Bank forecast that due to recovering oil prices inflation will start increasing gradually in the euro area and will become positive in the nearest months. Nevertheless, the average yearly inflation should remain low and account for only tenths of a percentage point.

TD 

Rokas Grajauskas, Danske Bank Analyst for the Baltic States, said that deflation is expected to last in Lithuania for at least several more months but in the second half of 2015 it will be shift to inflation. In the last months of 2015 inflation should gather momentum and reach 1.5 percent.

According to the analyst, prices of energy resources continue to be the primary factor which has dragged prices down. The average price of oil in January 2015 was merely USD 50 a barrel - more than twofold less than in January 2014, when it was at USD 107 a barrel.

The average price of oil in February 2015 increased to USD 59 a barrel. However, lower prices of petrol were observed in February but not in January because it takes several weeks to process and supply the final product.

Another reason that determined low inflation rates in Lithuania in February was the beginning of fierce competition of prices between major retail networks. In February prices of hundreds of products, including primary consumer goods, in main retail networks fell by 5-10 percent or more.

Karolis Broga

HD Danske Bank unit says insider information accusations dropped
WC 143 words
PD 13 March 2015
ET 08:36
SN Reuters News
SC LBA
LA English
CY Copyright 2015 Thomson Reuters. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

COPENHAGEN, March 13 (Reuters) - A Danish prosecutor has dropped accusations of unlawful disclosure of inside information against Danske Bank's mortgage unit, the head of the business said on Friday.

An employee in the mortgage unit, Realkredit Danmark, had been accused in July 2014 of giving insider information to an employee of Danske Bank's market division.

TD 

The accusation, which concerned a bond issue in 2009, followed another investigation into alleged price manipulation in Danske Bank.

Realkredit Danmark Chief Executive Carsten Nddebo Rasmussen said in a press release that both the insider information and price manipulation accusations had now been dropped.

There was no immediate comment from the office of Denmark's public prosecutor for serious economic and international crime. (Reporting By Alexander Tange; Editing by Keith Weir)

19 Mar 2015 03:30 ET *AP Moller-Maersk: Danske Share Offer Price Determined As Volume Weighted Avg Price From 20-26 March

19 Mar 2015 03:31 ET *AP Moller-Maersk: Danske Share Offer Price, Result Of Offering Expected 27 March

TD 

19 Mar 2015 03:32 ET *AP Moller-Maersk Previously Announced Plan to Offer Shareholders Opportunity to Acquire Co Stake in Danske Bank

19 Mar 2015 04:18 ET AP Moller-Maersk Announces Preliminary Terms of Danske Bank Share Sale

   By Dominic Chopping

Danish conglomerate A.P. Moller-Maersk A/S (MAERSK-A.KO) Thursday announced preliminary terms of its previously announced sale of Danske Bank A/S (DANSKE.KO) shares to its shareholders.

It said the offer price will be calculated as the volume weighted average price of Danske Bank shares between 20 March and 26 March, and both the offer price and result of the offering are expected to be announced on 27 March 2015.

Net proceeds from the offering will be used to cover, in whole or in part, financing of an extraordinary dividend and based on a pro forma offer price of DKK170 per Danske Bank share, estimated gross proceeds are seen at DKK34.38 billion ($4.93 billion).

As announced in the company's full-year report, shareholders will be entitled to order up to nine Danske Bank shares for each Maersk share held. Eligible shareholders will also be able to order any remaining Danske Bank shares not ordered by other shareholders, it said.

The offer period will start on 20 March and will close on 26 March.

HD Maersk gives terms for sale of Danske Bank stake
WC 148 words
PD 19 March 2015
ET 04:05
SN Reuters News
SC LBA
LA English
CY Copyright 2015 Thomson Reuters. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

COPENHAGEN, March 19 (Reuters) - Danish shipping and oil company A. P. Moller-Maersk on Thursday published the terms under which it will sell its 20 percent stake in Denmark's largest bank Danske Bank, a sale announced in February.

It said the offer price would be determined using a volume-weighted average price of Danske Bank shares traded between March 20 and March 26.

TD 

Based on a pro forma offer price of 170 crowns per share, estimated gross proceeds are 34.38 billion Danish crowns ($4.94 billion), if all shares are sold, Maersk said.

Maersk said in February it would sell 15 percent to its controlling shareholder, the Moller family foundation, and 5 percent to other existing shareholders.

($1 = 6.9652 Danish crowns) (Reporting by Teis Jensen; editing by Jason Neely)

HD Danske Bank predicts Norway rate cut in June, stronger crown
WC 209 words
PD 25 March 2015
ET 05:00
SN Reuters News
SC LBA
LA English
CY Copyright 2015 Thomson Reuters. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

OSLO, March 25 (Reuters) - The Norwegian central bank will probably cut its policy rate by 25 basis points in June to 1.0 percent and then remain on hold until late 2016, economists at Danske Bank predicted on Wednesday.

"The decline in oil investment is beginning to be noticed in the economy," the brokerage said, adding that "the worst is probably still to come though, with higher unemployment and more bankruptcies on the cards."

TD 

The central bank surprised investors by not delivering a widely anticipated rate cut at its March meeting, but said there would almost certainly be a cut to 1.0 percent by summer.

"Given that the market still expects two rate cuts and that we expect oil prices to stabilise in H1 15, we also expect the NOK to be stronger towards the end of the year than it is now," Danske Bank said.

The brokerage expects petroleum investments to drop by 14 percent this year and by another 4 percent next year, while mainland GDP growth is seen slowing to 1.7 percent in 2015 from 2.3 last year. (Reporting by Camilla Knudsen, editing by Terje Solsvik)

HD AP Moller-Maersk Offers Danske Bank Shares for Sale at DKK177.27
BY By Dominic Chopping
WC 184 words
PD 27 March 2015
ET 03:43
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright 2015, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

Danish conglomerate A.P. Moller-Maersk A/S (MAERSK-A.KO) said Friday that the offer period for the sale of its Danske Bank A/S (DANSKE.KO) stake ended yesterday with the offer price set at DKK177.27 per Danske Bank share.

TD 

Out of the 202,209,171 Danske Bank shares offered, 92% were ordered. A.P. Moller Holding A/S, who had made an undertaking to order 151,293,000 Danske Bank shares and declared an intention to order up to an additional 20,421,796 Danske Bank shares, has ordered 171,714,796 shares in total.

The extraordinary dividend is expected to amount to DKK1,671 per Maersk share.

If the extraordinary dividend is authorised and declared on 30 March 2015, the dividend will be paid on Tuesday, 7 April 2015 together with the ordinary dividend declared at the AGM.

HD Press Release: Fitch Affirms Realkredit Danmark's Capital Centres S & T Covered Bonds
WC 1454 words
PD 1 April 2015
ET 06:45
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright 2015, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

 
 
The following is a press release from Fitch Ratings :

Fitch Ratings -London-01 April 2015: Fitch Ratings has affirmed Realkredit Danmark A/S 's (Realkredit, A/Stable/F1, Viability Rating: a) mortgage covered bonds issued out of Capital Centre (CC) S at 'AAA', and CC T at 'AA+'. The Outlooks are Stable. The rating actions follow an annual review of the programmes. As of 31 December 2014, CC S had DKK226bn and CC T DKK431bn of covered bonds outstanding.

TD 

KEY RATING DRIVERS

- CC S covered bonds' rating is based on Realkredit's Long-term Issuer Default Rating (IDR) of 'A' , an unchanged Discontinuity Cap (D-Cap) of 3 (moderate high risk) and the 11.0% overcollateralisation (OC) that Fitch takes into account in its analysis, which provides more protection than the 8% 'AAA' breakeven OC.

CC T covered bonds' rating is based on Realkredit's Long-term IDR of 'A' , an unchanged D-Cap of 2 (high risk) and the 11.5% OC that Fitch takes into account in its analysis, which provides more protection than the 8% 'AA+' breakeven OC.

The Stable Outlook on the covered bonds' ratings is mainly driven by the Stable Outlook on Realkredit's IDR.

CC S 'AAA' breakeven OC has decreased to 8% from 10.5% and CC T 'AA+' breakeven OC to 8% from 11.5% due to: (i) a higher proportion of fixed rate assets for CC S and a larger proportion of assets with interest reset dates longer than one year in CC T; (ii) a reduction in Fitch's assumptions on the minimum probability of default (PD) applied to commercial assets (to 0.75% from 1%) to reflect the good historical performance of Realkredit's commercial assets. Notably, a large proportion of the loans in the portfolios are multifamily and cooperative housing, the performance of which has been stronger than the assets typically assessed under the SME CLO criteria to which the 1% is usually applied.

CC S and CC T cover assets contain 64% and 55% residential assets and 36% and 45% commercial assets, respectively. The residential mortgage loan asset analysis for both CCs was assessed using the Criteria Addendum - Denmark Residential Mortgage Loss and Cash Flow Assumptions', dated 12 December 2014. To ensure idiosyncratic risks are adequately protected against, the 'AAA' expected loss for CC S has been floored at 4% in line with Fitch's EMEA Residential Mortgage Loss Criteria dated 28 May 2014.

The breakeven OC for both covered bond programmes remains driven by the credit risk of the pool (9.5% at 'AAA' for CC S and 11.5% at 'AA+' for CCT) as Fitch does not model a fire sale of the assets in its cash flow analysis, but instead considers the possibility of bond refinancing post insolvency. However, in the recovery rate analysis, Fitch assumes that the cover pool would be sold below its par value. The breakeven OCs for the ratings are below the credit loss components because of the excess spread available in both CCs and because Fitch gives credit to recoveries for two notches above the tested rating on a PD basis.

The unchanged D-Caps are driven by the liquidity gap and systemic risk components, which are the weakest of the D-Cap components for both CCs, both of which are not fully protected against refinancing risk. Refinancing risk is higher in CC T, as it solely contains covered bonds without maturity matching assets. The risk is reducing over time since the change in legislation in March 2014 to include a mandatory maturity extension for bonds secured by mortgage loans with longer maturities than bonds. However, this provision only applies to bonds issued after March 2014.

Fitch currently provides no IDR uplift to the covered bonds as according to the European Bank Recovery and Resolution Directive (BRRD), covered bonds from specialised mortgage institutions that do not take deposits could bear losses in a resolution. However, Fitch will re-assess its position once the BRRD is implemented into Danish legislation.

RATING SENSITIVITIES

- The covered bonds' ratings would be vulnerable to a downgrade if any of the following occurred: (i) Realkredit's IDR was downgraded by one notch or more; or (ii) the D-Cap fell by one category or more; or (iii) the OC that Fitch takes into account in its analysis fell below 8% for CC S and 8% for CC T.

CC T covered bonds could be upgraded when more than 90% of the bonds have the new mandatory maturity extension feature as it will improve the liquidity risk.

The Fitch breakeven OC for the covered bond ratings will be affected, among others, by the profile of the cover assets relative to outstanding covered bonds, which can change over time, even in the absence of new issuance. Therefore the breakeven OC for the ratings cannot be assumed to remain stable over time.

More details on the cover pool and Fitch's analysis will be available in a credit update, which will shortly be available at www.fitchratings.com[http://www.fitchratings.com].

SE homeV2
HD Bloxhams Gunnell made bankrupt
BY Vincent Ryan
WC 341 words
PD 4 April 2015
ET 20:01
SN sundaytimes.co.uk
SC SUNDTI
LA English
CY  Times Newspapers Limited 2015

LP 

TADHG GUNNELL, the accountant at the centre of the collapse of Irelands oldest stockbroking firm, has been put into bankruptcy.

Gunnell, 39, with an address at Kempton Way, Navan Road Dublin, was ruled a bankrupt in Dublin on January 26, just weeks after Danske Bank had registered a 1.95m judgment against him.

TD 

Bloxham, which had been in business for more than 150 years, collapsed in May 2012. The Central Bank moved on the firm after it became apparent that the broker had been overstating its income for a number of years.

Gunnell was suspended immediately and a report by a firm of forensic accountants subsequently found that there was a 5.3m hole in the brokers accounts.

Gunnell joined Bloxham from Deloitte in 2000. He and six others personally borrowed sums from National Irish Bank (NIB) to fund a buyout of Bloxhams equity partners in 2007.

At the time of the collapse, the seven men managing partner Pramit Ghose; Niall Tinney, the former head of asset management; Paddy Finnegan, who headed private clients; Peter Costigan, head of institutional bonds; Raymond Deasy, partner institutional equities; Gunnell, the brokers former head of finance and compliance; and Patrick Dempsey, head of private clients were reported to have combined personal liability over 30m of debt owed to NIB.

Gunnell is the only partner to have had a judgment registered against him by Danske Bank, NIBs parent.

The High Court has listings this year for cases against Tinney, Finnegan, Costigan and Dempsey, who are defending Danskes claim. A case was also filed against Deasy, who contests the claim, while Ghose is understood to have settled with Danske.

At the time of the collapse, there was surprise that the Central Bank failed to pick up accounting errors over five years of audits, checks and inspections.

Following the collapse of Bloxham, it was reported that Gunnell had joined energy efficiency business Pinergy, set up by his brother Enda, a former partner at Mazars.

HD Denmark highlights naked truth about negative lending
BY Richard Milne
WC 753 words
PD 8 April 2015
ET 11:39
SN Financial Times (FT.Com)
SC FTCMA
LA English
CY Copyright 2015 The Financial Times Ltd. All rights reserved. Please do not cut and paste FT articles and redistribute by email or post to the web.

LP 

Eva Christiansen has become something of a star in Denmark. The sex therapist was propelled into the limelight not for her career but because of a loan she took from Realkredit Danmark, the country's biggest lender.

The reason? Ms Christiansen received a negative interest rate for her three-year loan, meaning the lender - part of Danske Bank - is paying for her to borrow money. The interest rate of minus 0.0172 per cent - which equates to her receiving about DKr7 each month from the bank - is just one sign of the "Through The Looking Glass" effects of extreme central banking measures in Scandinavia.

TD 

Plenty of central banks have resorted to unconventional measures such as buying government bonds. But none have gone quite so far as Sweden's Riksbank or Denmark's Nationalbank. The Riksbank became the first central bank in the world to take its main policy rate - the so-called repo rate - into negative territory. Nationalbanken in turn cut its deposit rate - the amount it pays or in this case charges banks for placing money with it - four times in three weeks at the start of this year to a world record low of minus 0.75 per cent.

Scandinavian bankers are under no illusions about the test such rates pose to the financial system. "We operate in exceptional times, where economic relationships are turned upside down with negative interest rates. A development that calls for caution; there is no history book to turn to," Annika Falkengren, chief executive of SEB, told shareholders at the Swedish bank's annual meeting.

A Danish banker is even more blunt: dealing with negative rates is like "learning to drive a car backwards". So far, however, the impact appears to have been manageable. Fears that negative rates could lead to widespread hoarding of cash or banks charging all customers for current accounts have proven wide of the mark.

Many Danish banks such as Danske have started charging their biggest corporate and institutional clients for depositing cash and Swedish lenders such as SEB have started discussions with similar clients. After all, if the banks themselves are having to pay 0.75 per cent - in Denmark's case - for depositing cash at the central bank, then it makes sense for those wanting to park large amounts of cash at lenders to share some of that burden. (The central bank has helped recently by greatly increasing the amount lenders can deposit before incurring a negative rate.)

But most banks have been careful to avoid charging the general public for current accounts. One exception was Erhvervsbank, a small Danish lender that said in February that it would charge 0.5 per cent on deposits. Larger lenders say they are keen to avoid any action that could encourage consumer cash hoarding.

Similarly, negative rates for loans have so far not become entrenched in Denmark, where many retail borrowers take out short-term loans of one or three years. Even Ms Christiansen will still pay the bank each month due to the fees on her loan. Recent auctions of short-term mortgage bonds unexpectedly had a positive interest rate. That in turn helped out some Danish banks, who had suggested they would suspend sales of new loans rather than issued at negative rates. At least part of the problem, according to bankers, was the financial equivalent of the Y2K problem - ensuring that banks' computers could deal with negative interest rates (just as many computers were supposed to have difficulties in dealing with the year 2000). Many are revamping their IT systems to ensure they can handle negative rates for borrowers and depositors.

But there is concern for what happens should negative rates persist for a long time. The biggest immediate concern is over whether low rates will fuel housing bubbles. Denmark, whose households are already the most indebted in the world, has seen prices in some parts of Copenhagen rise above their pre-crisis peak. In Sweden, the Riksbank remains deeply concerned about high levels of household debt being pushed up further.

Scandinavian bankers also say that the longer negative rates go on for, the more likely it is that normal consumers could be charged for depositing cash. As one says: "We just don't know how in the long run this will affect us. It is so completely new. But the longer it goes on, the more there is a risk for distortions."

richard.milne@ft.com

Twitter: @rmilneNordic

HD Danske Bank lends EUR 1.2 mln to Latvian fiberglass maker Valmieras SS
WC 234 words
PD 10 April 2015
ET 09:50
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Baltic News Service

LP 

RIGA, Apr 10, BNS - The Latvian branch of Danske Bank has granted a 1.203 million euros loan to Latvian fiberglass manufacturer Valmieras Stikla Skiedra (Valmieras SS), the company said in a statement to Nasdaq Riga stock exchange.

Valmieras SS representatives said that two contracts were concluded in March 2015 with Danke Bank on a loan for the purchase of precious metals, which Valmieras SS needs to increase its production capacity. The total value of the loan is 1.203 and the precious metals bought by Valmieras SS will serve as collateral.

TD 

The loan has to be repaid by March 2021.

The audited turnover of Valmieras Stikla Skiedra last year reached 91.7 million euros, growing 9.7 percent from a year before, and the company's profit was 7.028 million euros, up 46.3 percent rise from 2013. The Valmieras SS Group, meanwhile, generated 10.8.441 million euros in 2014 turnover, up 24 percent from 2013, and its profit rose 46.5 percent to 7.155 million euros.

The Latvian branch of Danske Bank became part of the Danish  Danske Bank Group in 2007. At the end of 2014, the Latvian branch of Danske Bank ranked 13th among the banks operating in Latvia in terms of assets.

Riga newsroom, +371 6708 8606, eko_zinas@bns.lv

LP 

STOCKHOLM--Swedish defense company Saab (SAAB-B.SK) said Thursday that it has signed a 2 billion krona ($227.9 million) multi-currency revolving credit facility.

The credit facility, which matures in 2020 with the possibility to extend, will be used for general corporate purposes and "strengthens Saab 's financial flexibility in connection with expansion," the company said.

TD 

The facility has been arranged by Skandinaviska Enskilda Banken AB , Credit Agricole Corporate and Investment Bank , Danske Bank AS , Nordea Bank AB , Swedbank AB , which each have a commitment of SEK400 million.

At 1505 GMT, shares traded down 2.9% at SEK232.20.

HD Insurer refuses to pay over alleged failure to disclose medical history
WC 209 words
PD 22 April 2015
SN The Irish Times
SC IRTI
PG 6
LA English
CY (c) 2015, The Irish Times.

LP 

An insurance company is refusing to pay out on a 250,000 mortgage protection policy because one of the policyholders, since deceased, failed to disclose her medical history, the High Court heard.

Marie McCabe died in August 2009, nearly four years after she and her husband, Joseph, took out the policy on a mortgage with National Irish Bank for their home in Ross, Mountnugent, Co Meath.

TD 

Irish Life Assurance is refusing to pay out over alleged material nondisclosure by Mrs McCabe of her medical history before taking out the policy.

Mr McCabe and his daughter Clara, who is her mother's personal representative, are suing Irish Life for breach of contract and negligence in refusing to pay out.

Mr Justice Anthony Barr ruled that Irish Life is not entitled to an order, in advance of the hearing of the case, requiring the McCabes to answer specific written questions in relation to the deceased's medical condition.

The McCabes argued there were no simple yes or no answers to the questions.

The issue was more complex and it would be necessary for the court to hear from two or three doctors who had treated Mrs McCabe, they argued.

   ASIAKASTIETO GROUP PLC STOCK EXCHANGE  RELEASE 24 APRIL 2015, 6.30 p.m. 
EET 
 
   Not for publication or distribution, directly or indirectly, in or into 
Australia, Canada, the Hong Kong special administrative region of the 
People's Republic of China, Japan, New Zealand, South Africa, Singapore 
or the United States, or any other jurisdiction in which the 
distribution or release would be unlawful. 
 
   Full exercise of over-allotment option and stabilisation in shares of 
Asiakastieto 
 
   Danske Bank A/S , Helsinki Branch ("Danske Bank "), the sole bookrunner in 
the share sale and personnel offering of Asiakastieto Group Plc  
("Asiakastieto"), has today decided on behalf of the Managers to fully 
exercise the over-allotment option granted to the Managers, Danske Bank  
and Pohjola Bank plc , by AKT Holdings S. r.l. ("AKT Holdings"). 
Danske Bank  purchases 1,725,000 shares in Asiakastieto from AKT Holdings 
and redelivers simultaneously to AKT Holdings the shares borrowed by 
Danske Bank  according to the Share Lending Agreement related to the 
share sale. 
 
   AKT Holdings has sold in the share sale a total of 13,225,000 shares in 
Asiakastieto, including the shares sold by exercise of the 
over-allotment option. The ownership of AKT Holdings in Asiakastieto 
after exercising the over-allotment option will be 1,775,000 shares, 
representing approximately 11.8 per cent of all outstanding shares in 
Asiakastieto. 
 
   Danske Bank  has carried out stabilisation measures in shares of 
Asiakastieto. Stabilisation was carried out on 9 April 2015 when 182 
shares were purchased at 14.75 euro per share. 
 
   The stabilisation period has been terminated today and no further 
stabilisation measures will be carried out. 
 
   Asiakastieto Group plc  
 
   Further enquiries 
 
   Jukka Ruuska , CEO, Asiakastieto Group Plc , Tel. +358 10 270 7111 
 
   About Asiakastieto 
 
   Asiakastieto is a leading Finnish provider of business and consumer 
information services. The Company's products and services are primarily 
used for risk management, decision-making and sales and marketing 
purposes. The Company believes that it is the market leader by revenue 
in credit information services in Finland. The Company also operates in 
the market for business and consumer information, as well as the market 
for sales and marketing information services in Finland. The Company has 
approximately 13,000 contract customers and its largest customers 
include financial institutions, insurance companies, telecommunication 
operators and wholesale and retail companies. In 2014, the Company's net 
sales totaled EUR 41.4 million with an adjusted EBIT of EUR 18.6 million,

148 people.

COPENHAGEN, April 29 (Reuters) - Denmark's biggest lender Danske Bank will cut around 50 positions from the corporate and institutions division of its investment bank in a bid to reduce costs, it told Reuters on Wednesday.

HD UPDATE 1-Danske Bank says to axe 50 jobs in its wholesale bank
WC 289 words
PD 29 April 2015
ET 09:54
SN Reuters News
SC LBA
LA English
CY Copyright 2015 Thomson Reuters. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

(Adds details)

COPENHAGEN, April 29 (Reuters) - Denmark's biggest lender Danske Bank will cut around 50 positions from its division that deals with corporate finance and trades instruments such as fixed income in an effort to reduce costs, it told Reuters on Wednesday.

TD 

Danske Bank, once the Nordic region's largest bank by market capitalisation, was particularly hard hit by Europe's financial crisis and has struggled to keep up with rivals on key metrics such as return on equity and allocated capital.

Analysts have said improving the Corporates & Institutions (C&I) business is key to the bank achieving its near-term group return on equity target of 9 percent by 2015 and a long-term target of 12 percent.

"This is part of an ongoing streamlining of the business to ensure our platform remains competitive," the head of Human Resources in C&I Danske Bank, Kristin Torgersen, wrote in an email.

Last year the bank cut 150 positions in the division, which by the end of 2014 employed 1,643 people. The C&I division made a profit before tax of 4.1 billion Danish crowns ($608 million) in 2014, 23 percent higher than in 2013.

Danske Bank will publish its first-quarter report on Thursday.

Reports from three of Denmark's top four banks - Jyske , Sydbank and Spar Nord - showed negative interest rates have been a boon for some Danish banks as a jump in fees from homeowners refinancing their mortgages offset the hit to interest income. ($1 = 6.7466 Danish crowns) (Reporting by Ole Mikkelsen; Editing by Sabina Zawadzki and Gareth Jones)

HD Danske Bank First-Quarter Net Profit Surges
BY By Anna Molin
WC 436 words
PD 30 April 2015
ET 02:40
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright 2015, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

Denmark's biggest lender, Danske Bank A/S (DANSKE.KO), Wednesday said increasing mortgage refinancing, higher trading income and lending growth helped drive a better-than-expected 73% rise in first quarter net profit.

TD 

Net profit at the Copenhagen-based bank rose to 4.83 billion Danish kroner ($713.8 million) in the three months to March 31, up from DKK2.79 billion in the year-earlier period and above an average DKK3.97 billion forecast by analysts in a FactSet poll.

Quarterly net interest income increased to DKK8.39 billion from DKK7.99 billion, as higher lending volumes offset pressure from negative interest rates on deposit margins.

Central banks in both Denmark and Sweden earlier this year slashed their interest rates into negative territory to keep their currencies from getting stronger, effectively making banks pay to park their excess cash. Part of that cost is being passed on to large institutional and corporate customers but most banks have so far balked at the idea of charging retail customers for deposits.

Analysts have feared that the negative rates would weigh heavily on interest income, but earnings reports this week show that most of the Scandinavian banks still managed to grow their profits. This is largely a result of higher fee and commissions income from re-mortgaging and increased customer demand for currency hedging and risk management products following high market volatility.

Danske Bank's earnings support that picture. Net fee income increased 19% as many of its customers took advantage of the ultralow interest rates and refinanced their mortgages, the bank said. Trading income soared to DKK11.44 billion from DKK2.36 billion, owing to high customer activity in the financial markets.

Loan impairment charges narrowed to DKK366 from DKK944 million.

"Although we have posted strong earnings, we maintain our guidance for the year because of considerable uncertainty about future interest rates, developments in the financial markets and the level of customer activity," Chief Executive Thomas E. Borgen said.

For 2015, the bank expects a net profit above DKK14 billion, total income around the same level as in 2014, expenses below DKK22 billion and impairment charges in its core activities to remain at a low level.

Danske said its common equity Tier 1 capital ratio--a measure of financial strength--stood at 14.1% at the end of the quarter, a tad higher than the 14.0% a year ago.

-Write to Anna Molin at anna.molin@wsj.com; Twitter: @AnnaWSJ

(END) Dow Jones Newswires

April 30, 2015 02:40 ET (06:40 GMT)

VILNIUS, Apr 30, BNS - The Lithuanian branch of Danske Bank, the second-biggest financial group in Northern Europe by assets, said on Thursday that its first-quarter net profit fell to 4.1 million euros, down 22.6 percent from 5.3 million euros in the same period last year.

The branch's pretax operating profit from core activities (business and retail banking) dropped by 6.4 percent to 4.4 million euros. It posted a loss of 0.7 million euros from non-core activities, versus a pretax profit of 0.9 million euros a year ago.

HD Latvian branch of Danske Bank posts EUR 551,000 profit for Q1
WC 543 words
PD 30 April 2015
ET 05:18
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Baltic News Service

LP 

RIGA, Apr 30, BNS - The Latvian branch of Danske Bank closed the first quarter of 2015 with a 551,000 euros profit in contrast to a loss incurred in the same period a year ago, the bank's spokeswoman Ieva Zauere told BNS.

Raivis Kakanis, the head of the Latvian branch of Danske Bank, reminded about the announcement made by the bank at the beginning of this year about plans to change the focus of its business operations in the Baltics. "In the future we will be concentrating on serving corporate clients and individual clients associated with these companies in order to provide them with individual services of the highest-quality and the best offers. During the first quarter of this year, Danske Bank continued to strengthen its position in serving corporate clients, the amount of loans granted to companies has grown by 53 percent over the past year," Kakanis said.

TD 

Zaure said that as a result of growing business operations the bank's operating revenue totaled 1.9 million euros in the first quarter of 2015, growing 45 percent year-on-year. Interes income grew 62 percent to 1.3 million euros, and commissions swelled 85 percent to 572,000 euros.

The bank's expenditure rose by 10 percent in the first three months of the year. "We already reported this year that the bank is going to invest in developing a single IT platform for Danske Bank in all three Baltic states. The Baltic IT platform will be largely integrated with the systems of the Danske Bank Group to ensure modern and uniform services for our corporate clients doing business in the Baltic states. We are planning to launch Danske Bank's single IT platform for the Baltic states by the end of 2016. In addition to that, we have also slightly increased the number of our employees," said Zauere.

The bank's representative also indicated that the bank's deposit portfolio expanded by 25 percent during the first three months of this year to 281 million euros. In the basic segment deposits grew by 40 percent. As a result of a 52 percent growth in corporate and related personal loans, the bank's total loan portfolio expanded by 24 percent to 374.3 million euros.

"In line with our strategy to concentrate on corporate clients, the loan portfolio of other individual clients continued to contract and decreased by 10 percent. Loans to companies grew by 53 percent to 246.7 million euros at the end of the first quarter. Danske Bank is determined to keep increasing its market share in the segment of corporate clients. We are currently working on a leasing service for our corporate clients, which will be launched by the end of this year," said Zauere.

The Latvian branch of Danske Bank reported a 7.648 million euros loss for the first quarter of 2014.

The Latvian branch of Danske Bank became part of the Danish Danske Bank Group in 2007. At the end of 2014, the Latvian branch of Danske Bank ranked 13th among the banks operating in Latvia in terms of assets.

Riga newsroom, +371 6708 8606, eko_zinas@bns.lv

HD Danske Bank Lithuania pre-tax profit at EUR 4.4mn in Q1
WC 346 words
PD 6 May 2015
SN Lithuanian News Agency - ELTA
SC ELTA
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Lithuanian News Agency - ELTA

LP 

Vilnius, May 6 (ELTA) - Danske Bank A/S Lithuania branch earned EUR 4.4 million on its core activities (business and private banking), and the bad debts' provisions decrease was EUR 1.2 million, the bank said in a statement.

In the first quarter of this year, both the core loan portfolio and core deposit portfolio rose 10 percent and 29 percent respectively, compared to the same period last year, in line with more optimistic business expectations.

TD 

"Despite the continuous geopolitical tension in the neighbouring markets, the main Lithuania's economic sectors are growing steadily, and this stimulates the entire country's economy. The most important thing is that Lithuania's business sector shows confidence in the future of our economy and maintains active by borrowing and launching new investment projects," says Gintautas Galvanauskas, CEO of Danske Bank Lithuania.

Positive business expectations are also reflected in economic forecasts. Despite the losses in the Russian market that is important to Lithuania, Danske Bank analytics forecast that the growth of Lithuania's economy will remain sustainable and will reach 2.5 percent. Moreover, it is expected to have even more active economic growth recovery. The growth is expected to be more rapid and reach up to 3.2 percent, by becoming independent from the Russian market and targeting export flows to other markets. Prospective of the next few years is the brightest in the entire European Union - the average pace of Lithuania's economy growth is expected to reach 3.4 percent until 2017.

"According to the renewed strategy of the Danske Bank Group, this year Baltic countries will continue paying particular attention to business and private banking customers. During the last year, the core loan portfolio increased by 10 percent and it shows that we can successfully reach and implement the ambitious goals of the new strategy. In the future we will consistently enhance the service in this segment and implement various banking service solutions for our customers," says Galvanauskas, the bank reported.

Irma Janiauskait
